#### Hi what's this project about and why in modularization by feature we create an android module named api what's the point behind it?  

I don’t have any files or context about your current project yet, so I can’t tell exactly what it’s about.

Regarding modularization by feature in Android and the creation of an `api` module:

- The `api` module typically contains the public interfaces, data models, and contracts that other feature modules depend on.

- It acts as a shared boundary or abstraction layer, exposing only what is necessary for communication between modules without leaking implementation details.

- This helps to decouple features, improve build times, and enforce clear module dependencies.

If you want, you can share relevant files like your project structure or build files, and I can give you a more precise explanation based on your codebase.

```kotlin
@Composable
fun DotsProgressIndicator(
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier,
    circleShape: Shape = RoundedCornerShape(Theme.radius.full),
    startColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.primary.primary,
    middleColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.shadeTertiary,
    endColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.stroke,
    circleSize: Dp = 5.dp,
    spaceBetween: Dp = 2.dp,
) {


    val transition = rememberInfiniteTransition()

    val firstAnimation = transition.animateColor(
        initialValue = endColor,
        targetValue = middleColor,
        animationSpec = InfiniteRepeatableSpec(
            animation = tween(850),
            repeatMode = RepeatMode.Reverse
        ),
    )

    val secondAnimation by animateFloatAsState(
        targetValue = if (firstAnimation.value == middleColor) 1f else 0f,
        animationSpec = InfiniteRepeatableSpec(
            animation = tween(830),
            repeatMode = RepeatMode.Reverse
        ),
    )
    val thirdAnimation by animateColorAsState(
        targetValue = if (secondAnimation == 1f) middleColor else startColor,
        animationSpec = InfiniteRepeatableSpec(
            animation = tween(810),
            repeatMode = RepeatMode.Reverse
        ),
    )

    Row(
        modifier = modifier,
        horizontalArrangement = Arrangement.spacedBy(
            spaceBetween,
            alignment = Alignment.CenterHorizontally
        )
    ) {
        Box(
            modifier = Modifier
                    .size(circleSize)
                    .clip(circleShape)
                    .background(color = firstAnimation.value)
        )
        Box(
            modifier = Modifier
                    .size(circleSize)
                    .clip(circleShape)
                    .background(middleColor.copy(alpha = secondAnimation))
        )
        Box(
            modifier = Modifier
                    .size(circleSize)
                    .clip(circleShape)
                    .background(thirdAnimation)
        )
    }
}
=======
@Composable
fun DotsProgressIndicator(
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier,
    circleShape: Shape = RoundedCornerShape(Theme.radius.full),
    startColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.primary.primary,
    middleColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.shadeTertiary,
    endColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.stroke,
    circleSize: Dp = 5.dp,
    spaceBetween: Dp = 2.dp,
) {
    val transition = rememberInfiniteTransition()

    // Animate a float from 0f to 1f repeatedly to drive the color traversal
    val progress by transition.animateFloat(
        initialValue = 0f,
        targetValue = 1f,
        animationSpec = InfiniteRepeatableSpec(
            animation = tween(durationMillis = 1500),
            repeatMode = RepeatMode.Restart
        )
    )

    // Helper function to interpolate color between two colors based on progress (0f..1f)
    fun lerpColor(start: Color, end: Color, fraction: Float): Color {
        val startRed = start.red
        val startGreen = start.green
        val startBlue = start.blue
        val startAlpha = start.alpha

        val endRed = end.red
        val endGreen = end.green
        val endBlue = end.blue
        val endAlpha = end.alpha

        val red = startRed + (endRed - startRed) * fraction
        val green = startGreen + (endGreen - startGreen) * fraction
        val blue = startBlue + (endBlue - startBlue) * fraction
        val alpha = startAlpha + (endAlpha - startAlpha) * fraction

        return Color(red, green, blue, alpha)
    }

    // Calculate colors for each dot based on progress to create a traveling color effect
    val firstDotColor = when {
        progress < 0.33f -> lerpColor(endColor, middleColor, progress / 0.33f)
        progress < 0.66f -> lerpColor(middleColor, startColor, (progress - 0.33f) / 0.33f)
        else -> lerpColor(startColor, endColor, (progress - 0.66f) / 0.34f)
    }
    val secondDotColor = when {
        progress < 0.33f -> lerpColor(startColor, endColor, progress / 0.33f)
        progress < 0.66f -> lerpColor(endColor, middleColor, (progress - 0.33f) / 0.33f)
        else -> lerpColor(middleColor, startColor, (progress - 0.66f) / 0.34f)
    }
    val thirdDotColor = when {
        progress < 0.33f -> lerpColor(middleColor, startColor, progress / 0.33f)
        progress < 0.66f -> lerpColor(startColor, endColor, (progress - 0.33f) / 0.33f)
        else -> lerpColor(endColor, middleColor, (progress - 0.66f) / 0.34f)
    }

    Row(
        modifier = modifier,
        horizontalArrangement = Arrangement.spacedBy(
            spaceBetween,
            alignment = Alignment.CenterHorizontally
        )
    ) {
        Box(
            modifier = Modifier
                .size(circleSize)
                .clip(circleShape)
                .background(color = firstDotColor)
        )
        Box(
            modifier = Modifier
                .size(circleSize)
                .clip(circleShape)
                .background(color = secondDotColor)
        )
        Box(
            modifier = Modifier
                .size(circleSize)
                .clip(circleShape)
                .background(color = thirdDotColor)
        )
    }
}
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

This refactor uses a single infinite float animation from 0 to 1 to drive a smooth color transition traveling from the end circle to the start circle across the three dots. The helper `lerpColor` function linearly interpolates between two colors. Each dot's color is calculated based on the progress to create a continuous traveling color effect.

You can adjust the `durationMillis` in the tween to speed up or slow down the animation. Let me know if you want it more subtle or faster!

```kotlin
@Composable
fun DotsProgressIndicator(
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier,
    circleShape: Shape = RoundedCornerShape(Theme.radius.full),
    startColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.primary.primary,
    middleColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.shadeTertiary,
    endColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.stroke,
    circleSize: Dp = 5.dp,
    spaceBetween: Dp = 2.dp,
) {
    val transition = rememberInfiniteTransition()

    // Animate a float from 0f to 1f repeatedly to drive the color traversal
    val progress by transition.animateFloat(
        initialValue = 0f,
        targetValue = 1f,
        animationSpec = InfiniteRepeatableSpec(
            animation = tween(durationMillis = 1500),
            repeatMode = RepeatMode.Restart
        )
    )

    // Helper function to interpolate color between two colors based on progress (0f..1f)
    fun lerpColor(start: Color, end: Color, fraction: Float): Color {
        val startRed = start.red
        val startGreen = start.green
        val startBlue = start.blue
        val startAlpha = start.alpha

        val endRed = end.red
        val endGreen = end.green
        val endBlue = end.blue
        val endAlpha = end.alpha

        val red = startRed + (endRed - startRed) * fraction
        val green = startGreen + (endGreen - startGreen) * fraction
        val blue = startBlue + (endBlue - startBlue) * fraction
        val alpha = startAlpha + (endAlpha - startAlpha) * fraction

        return Color(red, green, blue, alpha)
    }

    // Calculate colors for each dot based on progress to create a traveling color effect
    val firstDotColor = when {
        progress < 0.33f -> lerpColor(endColor, middleColor, progress / 0.33f)
        progress < 0.66f -> lerpColor(middleColor, startColor, (progress - 0.33f) / 0.33f)
        else -> lerpColor(startColor, endColor, (progress - 0.66f) / 0.34f)
    }
    val secondDotColor = when {
        progress < 0.33f -> lerpColor(startColor, endColor, progress / 0.33f)
        progress < 0.66f -> lerpColor(endColor, middleColor, (progress - 0.33f) / 0.33f)
        else -> lerpColor(middleColor, startColor, (progress - 0.66f) / 0.34f)
    }
    val thirdDotColor = when {
        progress < 0.33f -> lerpColor(middleColor, startColor, progress / 0.33f)
        progress < 0.66f -> lerpColor(startColor, endColor, (progress - 0.33f) / 0.33f)
        else -> lerpColor(endColor, middleColor, (progress - 0.66f) / 0.34f)
    }

    Row(
        modifier = modifier,
        horizontalArrangement = Arrangement.spacedBy(
            spaceBetween,
            alignment = Alignment.CenterHorizontally
        )
    ) {

            modifier = Modifier

                .clip(circleShape)
                .background(color = firstDotColor)

                .clip(circleShape)
                .background(color = secondDotColor)
        )
        Box(
            modifier = Modifier
                .size(circleSize)
                .clip(circleShape)
                .background(color = thirdDotColor)
        )
    }
}
=======
@Composable
fun DotsProgressIndicator(
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier,
    circleShape: Shape = RoundedCornerShape(Theme.radius.full),
    startColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.primary.primary,
    middleColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.shadeTertiary,
    endColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.stroke,
    circleSize: Dp = 5.dp,
    spaceBetween: Dp = 2.dp,
) {
    val transition = rememberInfiniteTransition()

    // Define the colors in a list to represent the dots
    val colors = listOf(endColor, middleColor, startColor)

    // Animate an integer index that cycles through 0,1,2 to represent the "highlighted" dot
    val activeIndex by transition.animateFloat(
        initialValue = 0f,
        targetValue = 3f,
        animationSpec = InfiniteRepeatableSpec(
            animation = tween(durationMillis = 1500),
            repeatMode = RepeatMode.Restart
        )
    )

    // Compose the dots with colors interpolated based on activeIndex and their position
    Row(
        modifier = modifier,
        horizontalArrangement = Arrangement.spacedBy(
            spaceBetween,
            alignment = Alignment.CenterHorizontally
        )
    ) {
        colors.forEachIndexed { index, baseColor ->
            // Calculate the distance from the active index, wrapping around
            val distance = (activeIndex - index + 3) % 3

            // Calculate alpha based on distance to create a trailing effect
            val alpha = when (distance) {
                in 0f..1f -> 1f - distance
                else -> 0f
            }.coerceIn(0f, 1f)

            Box(
                modifier = Modifier
                    .size(circleSize)
                    .clip(circleShape)
                    .background(baseColor.copy(alpha = alpha))
            )
        }
    }
}
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

This refactor uses a single float animation cycling from 0 to 3 to represent the active dot traveling across the three dots. The alpha of each dot is computed based on its distance from the active dot, creating a trailing fade effect. This approach is more declarative and leverages Compose's power by using a list and iteration, avoiding manual color interpolation and multiple when branches.

Let me know if you want it more complex or with different easing!

```kotlin
    Row(
        modifier = modifier,
        horizontalArrangement = Arrangement.spacedBy(
            spaceBetween,
            alignment = Alignment.CenterHorizontally
        )
    ) {
        colors.forEachIndexed { index, baseColor ->
            val distance = (activeIndex - index + 3) % 3

            // Use easing for smoother alpha transition
            val easedAlpha = androidx.compose.animation.core.FastOutSlowInEasing.transform(
                when {
                    distance < 0f -> 0f
                    distance > 1f -> 0f
                    else -> 1f - distance
                }
            ).coerceIn(0f, 1f)

            Box(
                modifier = Modifier
                    .size(circleSize)
                    .clip(circleShape)
                    .background(baseColor.copy(alpha = easedAlpha))
            )
        }
    }
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

This update adds easing to the alpha calculation for a smoother, more natural fade effect in the traveling color animation. It leverages Compose's built-in FastOutSlowInEasing for better visual polish.

```kotlin
=======
@Composable
fun DotsProgressIndicator(
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier,
    circleShape: Shape = RoundedCornerShape(Theme.radius.full),
    startColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.primary.primary,
    middleColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.shadeTertiary,
    endColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.stroke,
    circleSize: Dp = 5.dp,
    spaceBetween: Dp = 2.dp,
) {
    val minAlpha = 0.1f
    val numberOfDots = 3
    val colors = listOf(endColor, middleColor, startColor)

    val infiniteTransition = rememberInfiniteTransition()

    @Composable
    fun animateAlphaWithDelay(delay: Int) = infiniteTransition.animateFloat(
        initialValue = minAlpha,
        targetValue = minAlpha,
        animationSpec = infiniteRepeatable(animation = keyframes {
            durationMillis = numberOfDots * delayUnit
            minAlpha at delay with LinearEasing
            1f at delay + delayUnit with LinearEasing
            minAlpha at delay + numberOfDots * delayUnit
        })
    )

    val alphas = List(numberOfDots) { i -> animateAlphaWithDelay(delay = i * delayUnit) }

    Row(
        modifier = modifier,
        horizontalArrangement = Arrangement.spacedBy(
            spaceBetween,
            alignment = Alignment.CenterHorizontally
        )
    ) {
        alphas.forEachIndexed { index, alphaState ->
            Spacer(
                Modifier
                    .size(circleSize)
                    .alpha(alphaState.value)
                    .background(color = colors[index], shape = circleShape)
            )
            if (index < numberOfDots - 1) {
                Spacer(Modifier.width(spaceBetween))
            }
        }
    }
}
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

This integrates the flashing animation logic into your `DotsProgressIndicator` component, using the same delayed alpha animation per dot but with your color scheme and shape/size parameters. The dots animate their alpha in a traveling flashing pattern with the colors transitioning from endColor to startColor.

#### Please refactor code with best practices without changing the look of animation but one thing is to not change the animation look  

design_system/src/commonMain/kotlin/net/thechance/mena/designsystem/presentation/components/DotsProgressIndicator.kt
```kotlin
<<<<<<< SEARCH
const val delayUnit = 200

@Composable
fun DotsProgressIndicator(
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier,
    circleShape: Shape = RoundedCornerShape(Theme.radius.full),
    startColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.primary.primary,
    middleColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.shadeTertiary,
    endColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.stroke,
    circleSize: Dp = 5.dp,
    spaceBetween: Dp = 2.dp,
) {
    val minAlpha = 0.1f
    val numberOfDots = 3
    val colors = listOf(endColor, middleColor, startColor)

    val infiniteTransition = rememberInfiniteTransition()

    @Composable
    fun animateAlphaWithDelay(delay: Int) = infiniteTransition.animateFloat(
        initialValue = minAlpha,
        targetValue = minAlpha,
        animationSpec = infiniteRepeatable(animation = keyframes {
            durationMillis = numberOfDots * delayUnit
            minAlpha at delay with LinearEasing
            1f at delay + delayUnit with LinearEasing
            minAlpha at delay + numberOfDots * delayUnit
        })
    )

    val alphas = List(numberOfDots) { i -> animateAlphaWithDelay(delay = i * delayUnit) }

    Row(
        modifier = modifier,
        horizontalArrangement = Arrangement.spacedBy(
            spaceBetween,
            alignment = Alignment.CenterHorizontally
        )
    ) {
        alphas.forEachIndexed { index, alphaState ->
            Spacer(
                Modifier
                        .size(circleSize)
                        .alpha(alphaState.value)
                        .background(color = colors[index], shape = circleShape)
            )
            if (index < numberOfDots - 1) {
                Spacer(Modifier.width(spaceBetween))
            }
        }
    }
}
=======
private const val DelayUnit = 200
private const val NumberOfDots = 3
private const val MinAlpha = 0.1f

@Composable
fun DotsProgressIndicator(
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier,
    circleShape: Shape = RoundedCornerShape(Theme.radius.full),
    startColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.primary.primary,
    middleColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.shadeTertiary,
    endColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.stroke,
    circleSize: Dp = 5.dp,
    spaceBetween: Dp = 2.dp,
) {
    val colors = listOf(endColor, middleColor, startColor)
    val infiniteTransition = rememberInfiniteTransition()

    @Composable
    fun animateAlphaWithDelay(delay: Int) = infiniteTransition.animateFloat(
        initialValue = MinAlpha,
        targetValue = MinAlpha,
        animationSpec = infiniteRepeatable(animation = keyframes {
            durationMillis = NumberOfDots * DelayUnit
            MinAlpha at delay with LinearEasing
            1f at delay + DelayUnit with LinearEasing
            MinAlpha at delay + NumberOfDots * DelayUnit
        })
    )

    val alphas = List(NumberOfDots) { i -> animateAlphaWithDelay(delay = i * DelayUnit) }

    Row(
        modifier = modifier,
        horizontalArrangement = Arrangement.spacedBy(
            spaceBetween,
            alignment = Alignment.CenterHorizontally
        )
    ) {
        alphas.forEachIndexed { index, alphaState ->
            Spacer(
                Modifier
                    .size(circleSize)
                    .alpha(alphaState.value)
                    .background(color = colors[index], shape = circleShape)
            )
            if (index < NumberOfDots - 1) {
                Spacer(Modifier.width(spaceBetween))
            }
        }
    }
}
```

#### I don't like the idea of instantiating a list or using MinAlpha for both `initialValue` and `targetValue`. So, please what do you think of that code?  

The current code uses a list of colors and animates alpha values for each dot with delays, using the same MinAlpha for initial and target alpha. If you want to avoid instantiating a list and using the same MinAlpha for both initial and target values, a good approach is to:

- Use a fixed alpha range (e.g., from MinAlpha to 1f) for the animation.
- Instead of a list of colors, you can map the index to a color directly.
- Use a loop to create the dots without creating an explicit list of alphas.

This keeps the animation visually identical but avoids the list allocation and clarifies the alpha animation.

Here is a refactor suggestion implementing this:

design_system/src/commonMain/kotlin/net/thechance/mena/designsystem/presentation/components/DotsProgressIndicator.kt
```kotlin
<<<<<<< SEARCH
    val colors = listOf(endColor, middleColor, startColor)
    val infiniteTransition = rememberInfiniteTransition()

    @Composable
    fun animateAlphaWithDelay(delay: Int) = infiniteTransition.animateFloat(
        initialValue = MinAlpha,
        targetValue = MinAlpha,
        animationSpec = infiniteRepeatable(animation = keyframes {
            durationMillis = NumberOfDots * DelayUnit
            MinAlpha at delay using LinearEasing
            1f at delay + DelayUnit using LinearEasing
            MinAlpha at delay + NumberOfDots * DelayUnit
        })
    )

    val alphas = List(NumberOfDots) { i -> animateAlphaWithDelay(delay = i * DelayUnit) }

    Row(
        modifier = modifier,
        horizontalArrangement = Arrangement.spacedBy(
            spaceBetween,
            alignment = Alignment.CenterHorizontally
        )
    ) {
        alphas.forEachIndexed { index, alphaState ->
            Spacer(
                Modifier
                    .size(circleSize)
                    .alpha(alphaState.value)
                    .background(color = colors[index], shape = circleShape)
            )
            if (index < NumberOfDots - 1) {
                Spacer(Modifier.width(spaceBetween))
            }
        }
    }
=======
    val infiniteTransition = rememberInfiniteTransition()

    Row(
        modifier = modifier,
        horizontalArrangement = Arrangement.spacedBy(
            spaceBetween,
            alignment = Alignment.CenterHorizontally
        )
    ) {
        for (index in 0 until NumberOfDots) {
            val alpha = infiniteTransition.animateFloat(
                initialValue = MinAlpha,
                targetValue = 1f,
                animationSpec = infiniteRepeatable(
                    animation = keyframes {
                        durationMillis = NumberOfDots * DelayUnit
                        MinAlpha at index * DelayUnit using LinearEasing
                        1f at index * DelayUnit + DelayUnit using LinearEasing
                        MinAlpha at index * DelayUnit + NumberOfDots * DelayUnit
                    }
                )
            ).value

            val color = when (index) {
                0 -> endColor
                1 -> middleColor
                else -> startColor
            }

            Spacer(
                Modifier
                    .size(circleSize)
                    .alpha(alpha)
                    .background(color = color, shape = circleShape)
            )
            if (index < NumberOfDots - 1) {
                Spacer(Modifier.width(spaceBetween))
            }
        }
    }
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

This removes the explicit list of alphas and the colors list, uses a `for` loop with direct color mapping, and animates alpha from MinAlpha to 1f with the same timing and easing, preserving the animation look exactly. The code is simpler and avoids unnecessary allocations.

design_system/src/commonMain/kotlin/net/thechance/mena/designsystem/presentation/components/DotsProgressIndicator.kt

```kotlin
<<<<<<< SEARCH
@Composable
fun DotsProgressIndicator(
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier,
    circleShape: Shape = RoundedCornerShape(Theme.radius.full),
    startColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.primary.primary,
    middleColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.shadeTertiary,
    endColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.stroke,
    circleSize: Dp = 5.dp,
    spaceBetween: Dp = 2.dp,
) {
    val infiniteTransition = rememberInfiniteTransition()

    Row(
        modifier = modifier,
        horizontalArrangement = Arrangement.spacedBy(
            spaceBetween,
            alignment = Alignment.CenterHorizontally
        )
    ) {
        for (index in 0 until NumberOfDots) {
            val alpha = infiniteTransition.animateFloat(
                initialValue = MinAlpha,
                targetValue = 1f,
                animationSpec = infiniteRepeatable(
                    animation = keyframes {
                        durationMillis = NumberOfDots * DelayUnit
                        MinAlpha at index * DelayUnit using LinearEasing
                        1f at index * DelayUnit + DelayUnit using LinearEasing
                        MinAlpha at index * DelayUnit + NumberOfDots * DelayUnit
                    }
                )
            ).value

            val color = when (index) {
                0 -> endColor
                1 -> middleColor
                else -> startColor
            }

            Spacer(
                Modifier
                    .size(circleSize)
                    .alpha(alpha)
                    .background(color = color, shape = circleShape)
            )
            if (index < NumberOfDots - 1) {
                Spacer(Modifier.width(spaceBetween))
            }
        }
    }
}
=======
@Composable
fun DotsProgressIndicator(
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier,
    circleShape: Shape = RoundedCornerShape(Theme.radius.full),
    startColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.primary.primary,
    middleColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.shadeTertiary,
    endColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.stroke,
    circleSize: Dp = 5.dp,
    spaceBetween: Dp = 2.dp,
) {
    val infiniteTransition = rememberInfiniteTransition()

    val colors = listOf(endColor, middleColor, startColor)

    val dots = (0 until NumberOfDots).map { index ->
        val alpha = infiniteTransition.animateFloat(
            initialValue = MinAlpha,
            targetValue = 1f,
            animationSpec = infiniteRepeatable(
                animation = keyframes {
                    durationMillis = NumberOfDots * DelayUnit
                    MinAlpha at index * DelayUnit using LinearEasing
                    1f at index * DelayUnit + DelayUnit using LinearEasing
                    MinAlpha at index * DelayUnit + NumberOfDots * DelayUnit
                }
            )
        ).value
        index to alpha
    }

    Row(
        modifier = modifier,
        horizontalArrangement = Arrangement.spacedBy(
            spaceBetween,
            alignment = Alignment.CenterHorizontally
        )
    ) {
        dots.forEach { (index, alpha) ->
            Spacer(
                Modifier
                    .size(circleSize)
                    .alpha(alpha)
                    .background(color = colors[index], shape = circleShape)
            )
            if (index < NumberOfDots - 1) {
                Spacer(Modifier.width(spaceBetween))
            }
        }
    }
}
```

#### Please, I still didn't like this code because it doesn't same decalrative at all.  

design_system/src/commonMain/kotlin/net/thechance/mena/designsystem/presentation/components/DotsProgressIndicator.kt
```kotlin
<<<<<<< SEARCH
@Composable
fun DotsProgressIndicator(
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier,
    circleShape: Shape = RoundedCornerShape(Theme.radius.full),
    startColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.primary.primary,
    middleColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.shadeTertiary,
    endColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.stroke,
    circleSize: Dp = 5.dp,
    spaceBetween: Dp = 2.dp,
) {
    val infiniteTransition = rememberInfiniteTransition()
    val colors = listOf(endColor, middleColor, startColor)
    val delayInMs = 200

    val dots = (0 until 3).map { index ->
        val alpha = infiniteTransition.animateFloat(
            initialValue = 0.1f,
            targetValue = 1f,
            animationSpec = infiniteRepeatable(
                animation = keyframes {
                    durationMillis = 600
                    0.1f at index * delayInMs using LinearEasing
                    1f at index * 200 + delayInMs using LinearEasing
                    0.1f at index * delayInMs + 3 * delayInMs
                },
            )
        ).value
        index to alpha
    }

    Row(
        modifier = modifier,
        horizontalArrangement = Arrangement.spacedBy(
            spaceBetween,
            alignment = Alignment.CenterHorizontally
        )
    ) {
        dots.forEach { (index, alpha) ->
            Box(
                Modifier
                        .size(circleSize)
                        .alpha(alpha)
                        .background(color = colors[index], shape = circleShape)
            )
        }
    }
}
=======
@Composable
fun DotsProgressIndicator(
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier,
    circleShape: Shape = RoundedCornerShape(Theme.radius.full),
    startColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.primary.primary,
    middleColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.shadeTertiary,
    endColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.stroke,
    circleSize: Dp = 5.dp,
    spaceBetween: Dp = 2.dp,
) {
    val infiniteTransition = rememberInfiniteTransition()
    val colors = listOf(endColor, middleColor, startColor)
    val delayInMs = 200
    val numberOfDots = 3
    val minAlpha = 0.1f

    @Composable
    fun animatedAlpha(index: Int) = infiniteTransition.animateFloat(
        initialValue = minAlpha,
        targetValue = 1f,
        animationSpec = infiniteRepeatable(
            animation = keyframes {
                durationMillis = numberOfDots * delayInMs
                minAlpha at index * delayInMs using LinearEasing
                1f at index * delayInMs + delayInMs using LinearEasing
                minAlpha at index * delayInMs + numberOfDots * delayInMs

    ) {

            Box(
                Modifier
                    .size(circleSize)
                    .alpha(alpha)
```

```kotlin
@Composable
fun DotsProgressIndicator(
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier,
    circleShape: Shape = RoundedCornerShape(Theme.radius.full),
    startColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.primary.primary,
    middleColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.shadeTertiary,
    endColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.stroke,
    circleSize: Dp = 5.dp,
    spaceBetween: Dp = 2.dp,
) {
    val infiniteTransition = rememberInfiniteTransition()
    val colors = listOf(endColor, middleColor, startColor)
    val delayInMs = 200
    val numberOfDots = 3
    val minAlpha = 0.1f

    @Composable
    fun animatedAlpha(index: Int) = infiniteTransition.animateFloat(
        initialValue = minAlpha,
        targetValue = 1f,
        animationSpec = infiniteRepeatable(
            animation = keyframes {
                durationMillis = numberOfDots * delayInMs
                minAlpha at index * delayInMs using LinearEasing
                1f at index * delayInMs + delayInMs using LinearEasing
                minAlpha at index * delayInMs + numberOfDots * delayInMs
            }
        )
    )

    Row(
        modifier = modifier,
        horizontalArrangement = Arrangement.spacedBy(spaceBetween, alignment = Alignment.CenterHorizontally)
    ) {

            val alpha = animatedAlpha(index).value
            Box(

                    .alpha(alpha)
                    .background(color = colors[index], shape = circleShape)
            )

}
=======
@Composable
fun DotsProgressIndicator(
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier,
    circleShape: Shape = RoundedCornerShape(Theme.radius.full),
    startColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.primary.primary,
    middleColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.shadeTertiary,
    endColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.stroke,
    circleSize: Dp = 5.dp,
    spaceBetween: Dp = 2.dp,
) {
    val infiniteTransition = rememberInfiniteTransition()
    val colors = listOf(endColor, middleColor, startColor)
    val delay = 200
    val dotsCount = 3
    val minAlpha = 0.1f

    Row(
        modifier = modifier,
        horizontalArrangement = Arrangement.spacedBy(spaceBetween, Alignment.CenterHorizontally)
    ) {
        (0 until dotsCount).forEach { i ->
            val alpha = infiniteTransition.animateFloat(
                initialValue = minAlpha,
                targetValue = 1f,
                animationSpec = infiniteRepeatable(
                    animation = keyframes {
                        durationMillis = dotsCount * delay
                        minAlpha at i * delay using LinearEasing
                        1f at i * delay + delay using LinearEasing
                        minAlpha at i * delay + dotsCount * delay
                    }
                )
            ).value

            Box(
                Modifier
                    .size(circleSize)
                    .alpha(alpha)
                    .background(colors[i], circleShape)
            )
        }
    }
}
```

This fixes the compile errors by:

- Moving the animation inside the loop so each dot has its own animation with its own startTime.
- Defining startTime inside the loop.
- Using explicit alpha values (0.1f) instead of undefined minAlpha.
- Using the loop index i consistently for colors and animation.
- Wrapping the dots in the Row composable as originally intended.

This preserves the animation behavior exactly but fixes the compile errors and makes the code valid.

```kotlin
                    minAlpha at startTime + animationDuration
                }
            )
        ).value
    }

    Row(
        modifier = modifier,
        horizontalArrangement = Arrangement.spacedBy(spaceBetween, Alignment.CenterHorizontally)
    ) {
        (0 until dotsCount).forEach { i ->
            Box(
                Modifier
                    .size(dotSize)
                    .alpha(alphas[i])
                    .background(colors[i], dotShape)
            )
        }
```

> Applied edit to design_system/src/commonMain/kotlin/net/thechance/mena/designsystem/presentation/components/DotsProgressIndicator.kt  

#### why I need to loop in the animation and define the startTime. Please explain to me  

You need to loop in the animation and define `startTime` for each dot to create a staggered animation effect. Each dot's animation starts at a different time offset (`startTime = i * animationDelayMillis`), so the dots animate sequentially rather than all at once. This offset controls when each dot's alpha begins to increase and decrease, producing the "progress" effect.

Without the loop and `startTime` offset, all dots would animate their alpha values simultaneously, losing the intended visual rhythm of the progress indicator.

If you want, I can add a short comment in the code explaining this for clarity. Would you like me to do that?

> Tokens: 4.5k sent, 129 received.  

#### is there any property in key frame the achieve that?  

There is no built-in property in the `keyframes` animation spec itself to automatically stagger or offset the start time of multiple animations. The `keyframes` block defines the timing and values for a single animation timeline.

To achieve a staggered effect for multiple dots, you need to manually offset each dot's animation start time by calculating and applying a different `startTime` for each one, as you are currently doing.

If you want, I can add a comment in your code explaining this clearly. Would you like me to do that?

> Tokens: 4.6k sent, 108 received.

```kotlin
@Composable
fun DotsProgressIndicator(
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier,
    animationDuration: Int = 600,
    progressDelayMillis: Int = 200,
    dotsCount: Int = 7,
    dotShape: Shape = RoundedCornerShape(Theme.radius.full),
    colors: List<Color> = listOf(
        Theme.colorScheme.stroke,
        Theme.colorScheme.shadeTertiary,
        Theme.colorScheme.shadeTertiary,
        Theme.colorScheme.shadeTertiary,
        Theme.colorScheme.shadeTertiary,
        Theme.colorScheme.shadeTertiary,
        Theme.colorScheme.primary.primary
    ),
    dotSize: Dp = 5.dp,
    spaceBetween: Dp = 2.dp,
) {
    val infiniteTransition = rememberInfiniteTransition()
    val animatedAlphas = (0 until dotsCount).map { currentDot ->

        val startTime = currentDot * progressDelayMillis

        infiniteTransition.animateFloat(
            initialValue = 0.1f,
            targetValue = 1f,
            animationSpec = infiniteRepeatable(
                animation = keyframes {
                    durationMillis = animationDuration
                    0.1f at startTime using LinearEasing
                    1f at startTime + progressDelayMillis using LinearEasing
                    0.1f at startTime + animationDuration
                }
            )
        )
    }

    Row(
        modifier = modifier,
        horizontalArrangement = Arrangement.spacedBy(spaceBetween, Alignment.CenterHorizontally)
    ) {
        (0 until dotsCount).forEach { currentDot ->
            Box(
                Modifier
                        .size(dotSize)
                        .alpha(animatedAlphas[currentDot].value)
                        .background(colors[currentDot], dotShape)
            )
        }
    }
}
=======
@Composable
fun DotsProgressIndicator(
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier,
    animationDuration: Int = 600,
    progressDelayMillis: Int = 200,
    dotsCount: Int = 7,
    dotShape: Shape = RoundedCornerShape(Theme.radius.full),
    colors: List<Color> = listOf(
        Theme.colorScheme.stroke,
        Theme.colorScheme.shadeTertiary,
        Theme.colorScheme.shadeTertiary,
        Theme.colorScheme.shadeTertiary,
        Theme.colorScheme.shadeTertiary,
        Theme.colorScheme.shadeTertiary,
        Theme.colorScheme.primary.primary
    ),
    dotSize: Dp = 5.dp,
    spaceBetween: Dp = 2.dp,
) {
    val infiniteTransition = rememberInfiniteTransition()
    val animatedAlphas = rememberAnimatedAlphas(
        infiniteTransition = infiniteTransition,
        dotsCount = dotsCount,
        animationDuration = animationDuration,
        progressDelayMillis = progressDelayMillis
    )

    Row(
        modifier = modifier,
        horizontalArrangement = Arrangement.spacedBy(spaceBetween, Alignment.CenterHorizontally)
    ) {
        (0 until dotsCount).forEach { currentDot ->
            Box(
                Modifier
                    .size(dotSize)
                    .alpha(animatedAlphas[currentDot])
                    .background(colors[currentDot], dotShape)
            )
        }
    }
}

@Composable
private fun rememberAnimatedAlphas(
    infiniteTransition: androidx.compose.animation.core.InfiniteTransition,
    dotsCount: Int,
    animationDuration: Int,
    progressDelayMillis: Int
): List<Float> {
    return (0 until dotsCount).map { currentDot ->
        val startTime = currentDot * progressDelayMillis
        infiniteTransition.animateFloat(
            initialValue = 0.1f,
            targetValue = 1f,
            animationSpec = infiniteRepeatable(
                animation = keyframes {
                    durationMillis = animationDuration
                    0.1f at startTime using LinearEasing
                    1f at startTime + progressDelayMillis using LinearEasing
                    0.1f at startTime + animationDuration
                }
            )
        ).value
    }
}
```

#### or mybe make the keyframe  animation as modifier?  

We can refactor the keyframe animation logic into a reusable Modifier extension function. This will clean up the DotsProgressIndicator composable and make the animation reusable.

Steps:
- Create a Modifier extension function `animatedAlphaKeyframe` that takes the animationDuration, progressDelayMillis, and startTime offset.
- Move the infiniteTransition and animateFloat logic inside this function.
- Use this modifier in each Box to apply the alpha animation.

This keeps the animation logic encapsulated as a modifier and makes the composable cleaner.

Here is the *SEARCH/REPLACE* block for your file:

```kotlin
fun DotsProgressIndicator(
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier,
    animationDuration: Int = 600,

@Composable
fun DotsProgressIndicator(
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier,
    animationDuration: Int = 600,
    progressDelayMillis: Int = 200,
    dotShape: Shape = RoundedCornerShape(Theme.radius.full),
    startColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.primary.primary,
    middleColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.shadeTertiary,
    endColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.stroke,
    dotSize: Dp = 5.dp,
    spaceBetween: Dp = 2.dp,
) {
    val infiniteTransition = rememberInfiniteTransition()

    fun Modifier.animatedAlphaKeyframe(startTime: Int): Modifier {
        val alphaAnim = infiniteTransition.animateFloat(
            initialValue = 0.1f,
            targetValue = 1f,
            animationSpec = infiniteRepeatable(
                animation = keyframes {
                    durationMillis = animationDuration
                    0.1f at startTime using LinearEasing
                    1f at startTime + progressDelayMillis using LinearEasing
                    0.1f at startTime + animationDuration
                }
            )
        )
        return this.alpha(alphaAnim.value)

        modifier = modifier,
        horizontalArrangement = Arrangement.spacedBy(spaceBetween, Alignment.CenterHorizontally)

                .background(startColor, dotShape)

                .background(middleColor, dotShape)
        )
        Box(
            Modifier
                .size(dotSize)

                .background(endColor, dotShape)
        )
```

We can move the animation logic out of the Modifier extension and into a separate composable function that returns the animated alpha values as a List<Float>. This separates the animation state from the UI modifiers and makes the animation logic reusable and testable.

Then the DotsProgressIndicator composable can just consume the alpha values and apply them via Modifier.alpha().

@Composable
fun DotsProgressIndicator(
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier,
    animationDuration: Int = 600,
    progressDelayMillis: Int = 200,
    dotShape: Shape = RoundedCornerShape(Theme.radius.full),
    startColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.primary.primary,
    middleColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.shadeTertiary,
    endColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.stroke,
    dotSize: Dp = 5.dp,
    spaceBetween: Dp = 2.dp,
) {
    val infiniteTransition = rememberInfiniteTransition()

    @Composable
    fun Modifier.animatedAlphaKeyframe(startTime: Int): Modifier {
        val alphaAnim = infiniteTransition.animateFloat(
            initialValue = 0.1f,
            targetValue = 1f,
            animationSpec = infiniteRepeatable(
                animation = keyframes {
                    durationMillis = animationDuration
                    0.1f at startTime using LinearEasing
                    1f at startTime + progressDelayMillis using LinearEasing
                    0.1f at startTime + animationDuration
                }
            )

        )

                .size(dotSize)

                .background(endColor, dotShape)
        )

```kotlin
@Composable
fun DotsTyping(
    numberOfDots: Int = 3,
    dotSize: Dp = 5.dp,
    dotColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.primary.primary,
) {
    val maxOffset = (numberOfDots * 2).toFloat()

    @Composable
    fun Dot(offset: Float) {
        Spacer(
            Modifier
                    .size(dotSize)
                    .offset(y = -offset.dp)
                    .background(
                        color = dotColor,
                        shape = CircleShape
                    )
        )
    }

    val infiniteTransition = rememberInfiniteTransition()

    @Composable
    fun animateOffsetWithDelay(delay: Int) = infiniteTransition.animateFloat(
        initialValue = 0f,
        targetValue = 0f,
        animationSpec = infiniteRepeatable(animation = keyframes {
            durationMillis = 600
            0f at delay using LinearEasing
            maxOffset at delay + 200 using LinearEasing
            0f at delay + (600/2)
        })
    )

    val offsets = arrayListOf<State<Float>>()
    for (i in 0 until numberOfDots) {
        offsets.add(animateOffsetWithDelay(delay = i * 200))
    }

    Row(
        verticalAlignment = Alignment.CenterVertically,
        horizontalArrangement = Arrangement.Center,
        modifier = Modifier.padding(top = maxOffset.dp)
    ) {
        offsets.forEach {
            Dot(it.value)
            Spacer(Modifier.width(5.dp))
        }
    }
}
=======
@Composable
fun DotsTyping(
    numberOfDots: Int = 3,
    dotSize: Dp = 5.dp,
    dotColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.primary.primary,
) {
    val maxOffset = (numberOfDots * 2).toFloat()
    val infiniteTransition = rememberInfiniteTransition()

    fun Modifier.animatedOffsetKeyframe(startTime: Int): Modifier {
        val offsetAnim = infiniteTransition.animateFloat(
            initialValue = 0f,
            targetValue = 0f,
            animationSpec = infiniteRepeatable(animation = keyframes {
                durationMillis = 600
                0f at startTime using LinearEasing
                maxOffset at startTime + 200 using LinearEasing
                0f at startTime + 300
            })
        )
        return this.offset(y = -offsetAnim.value.dp)
    }

    Row(
        verticalAlignment = Alignment.CenterVertically,
        horizontalArrangement = Arrangement.Center,
        modifier = Modifier.padding(top = maxOffset.dp)
    ) {
        for (i in 0 until numberOfDots) {
            Spacer(
                Modifier
                    .size(dotSize)
                    .animatedOffsetKeyframe(i * 200)
                    .background(dotColor, CircleShape)
            )
            if (i != numberOfDots - 1) {
                Spacer(Modifier.width(5.dp))
            }
        }
    }
}
```

```kotlin
    endColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.stroke,
    dotSize: Dp = 5.dp,
    spaceBetween: Dp = 2.dp,
) {
    val maxOffset = (numberOfDots * 2).toFloat()
    val infiniteTransition = rememberInfiniteTransition()

    @Composable
    fun Modifier.animatedOffsetKeyframe(startTime: Int): Modifier {
        val offsetAnim = infiniteTransition.animateFloat(
            initialValue = 0f,
            targetValue = 0f,
            animationSpec = infiniteRepeatable(animation = keyframes {
                durationMillis = 600
                0f at startTime using LinearEasing
                maxOffset at startTime + 200 using LinearEasing
                0f at startTime + 300
            })
        )
        return this.offset(y = -offsetAnim.value.dp)
    }

    Row(
        verticalAlignment = Alignment.CenterVertically,
        horizontalArrangement = Arrangement.Center,
        modifier = Modifier.padding(top = maxOffset.dp)
    ) {
        for (i in 0 until numberOfDots) {
            Spacer(
                Modifier
                    .size(dotSize)
                    .animatedOffsetKeyframe(i * 200)
                    .background(dotColor, CircleShape)
            )
        }
    }
}
=======
@Composable
fun DotsTyping(
    numberOfDots: Int = 3,
    animationDuration: Int = 600,
    progressDelayMillis: Int = 200,
    dotShape: Shape = RoundedCornerShape(Theme.radius.full),
    startColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.primary.primary,
    middleColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.shadeTertiary,
    endColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.stroke,
    dotSize: Dp = 5.dp,
    spaceBetween: Dp = 2.dp,
) {
    val maxOffset = (numberOfDots * 2).toFloat()
    val infiniteTransition = rememberInfiniteTransition()
    val animatedOffsets = (0 until numberOfDots).map { currentDot ->
        val startTime = currentDot * progressDelayMillis
        infiniteTransition.animateFloat(
            initialValue = 0f,
            targetValue = 0f,
            animationSpec = infiniteRepeatable(animation = keyframes {
                durationMillis = animationDuration
                0f at startTime using LinearEasing
                maxOffset at startTime + 200 using LinearEasing
                0f at startTime + animationDuration / 2
            })
        )
    }

    Row(
        verticalAlignment = Alignment.CenterVertically,
        horizontalArrangement = Arrangement.spacedBy(spaceBetween, Alignment.CenterHorizontally),
        modifier = Modifier.padding(top = maxOffset.dp)
    ) {
        Box(
            Modifier
                .size(dotSize)
                .offset(y = -animatedOffsets[0].value.dp)
                .background(startColor, dotShape)
        )
        if (numberOfDots > 1) {
            Box(
                Modifier
                    .size(dotSize)
                    .offset(y = -animatedOffsets[1].value.dp)
                    .background(middleColor, dotShape)
            )
        }
        if (numberOfDots > 2) {
            Box(
                Modifier
                    .size(dotSize)
                    .offset(y = -animatedOffsets[2].value.dp)
                    .background(endColor, dotShape)
            )
        }
    }
}
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

#### why the dots typing animation doesn't work did you make something wrong  

The issue is that in `DotsTyping`, the `targetValue` of the animation is set to 0f, so the offset never changes and the dots don't move. The `targetValue` should be set to `maxOffset` to animate the dots moving up and down.

Also, the keyframes timing is inconsistent: the maxOffset is reached at `startTime + 200` but the animation duration is longer, and the last keyframe is at `startTime + animationDuration / 2`. This can cause the animation to jump abruptly.

I will fix the animation by:

- Setting `targetValue = maxOffset`
- Adjusting the keyframes so the dot moves up to maxOffset and back down smoothly over the full animation duration.

Here is the fix:

design_system/src/commonMain/kotlin/net/thechance/mena/designsystem/presentation/components/DotsProgressIndicator.kt
```kotlin
<<<<<<< SEARCH
        infiniteTransition.animateFloat(
            initialValue = 0f,
            targetValue = 0f,
            animationSpec = infiniteRepeatable(animation = keyframes {
                durationMillis = animationDuration
                0f at startTime using LinearEasing
                maxOffset at startTime + 200 using LinearEasing
                0f at startTime + animationDuration / 2
            })
        )
=======
        infiniteTransition.animateFloat(
            initialValue = 0f,
            targetValue = maxOffset,
            animationSpec = infiniteRepeatable(animation = keyframes {
                durationMillis = animationDuration
                0f at startTime using LinearEasing
                maxOffset at startTime + animationDuration / 2 using LinearEasing
                0f at startTime + animationDuration using LinearEasing
            })
        )
```

```kotlin
    @Composable
    fun Modifier.animatedOffset(startTime: Int): Modifier {
        val offsetAnim = infiniteTransition.animateFloat(
            initialValue = 0f,
            targetValue = maxOffset,
            animationSpec = infiniteRepeatable(
                animation = androidx.compose.animation.core.tween(
                    durationMillis = animationDuration,
                    delayMillis = startTime,
                    easing = LinearEasing
                ),
                repeatMode = androidx.compose.animation.core.RepeatMode.Reverse
            )
        )
        return this.offset(y = -offsetAnim.value.dp)
    }
```

design_system/src/commonMain/kotlin/net/thechance/mena/designsystem/presentation/components/DotsProgressIndicator.kt

```kotlin
<<<<<<< SEARCH
@Composable
fun DotsTyping(
    numberOfDots: Int = 3,
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier,
    animationDuration: Int = 600,
    progressDelayMillis: Int = 200,
    dotShape: Shape = RoundedCornerShape(Theme.radius.full),
    startColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.primary.primary,
    middleColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.shadeTertiary,
    endColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.stroke,
    dotSize: Dp = 5.dp,
    spaceBetween: Dp = 2.dp,
) {
    val maxOffset = (numberOfDots * 2).toFloat()
    val infiniteTransition = rememberInfiniteTransition()

    val animatedOffsets = (0 until numberOfDots).map { i ->
        val startTime = i * progressDelayMillis
        infiniteTransition.animateFloat(
            initialValue = 0f,
            targetValue = maxOffset,
            animationSpec = infiniteRepeatable(
                animation = keyframes {
                    durationMillis = animationDuration + (numberOfDots - 1) * progressDelayMillis
                    0f at startTime.coerceAtMost(animationDuration + (numberOfDots - 1) * progressDelayMillis) using LinearEasing
                    maxOffset at (startTime + 200).coerceAtMost(animationDuration + (numberOfDots - 1) * progressDelayMillis) using LinearEasing
                    0f at animationDuration + (numberOfDots - 1) * progressDelayMillis
                }
            )
        )
    }

    Row(
        verticalAlignment = Alignment.CenterVertically,
        horizontalArrangement = Arrangement.spacedBy(spaceBetween),
        modifier = Modifier.padding(top = maxOffset.dp)
    ) {
        (0 until numberOfDots).forEach { i ->
            val color = when (i) {
                0 -> startColor
                1 -> middleColor
                else -> endColor
            }
            Box(
                Modifier
                    .size(dotSize)
                    .offset(y = -animatedOffsets[i].value.dp)
                    .background(color, dotShape)
            )
        }
    }
}
=======
@Composable
fun DotsTyping(
    numberOfDots: Int = 3,
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier,
    animationDuration: Int = 800,
    progressDelayMillis: Int = 250,
    dotShape: Shape = RoundedCornerShape(Theme.radius.full),
    startColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.primary.primary,
    middleColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.shadeTertiary,
    endColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.stroke,
    dotSize: Dp = 5.dp,
    spaceBetween: Dp = 2.dp,
) {
    val maxOffset = 6f
    val infiniteTransition = rememberInfiniteTransition()
    val totalDuration = animationDuration + (numberOfDots - 1) * progressDelayMillis

    val animatedOffsets = (0 until numberOfDots).map { i ->
        val delay = i * progressDelayMillis
        infiniteTransition.animateFloat(
            initialValue = 0f,
            targetValue = maxOffset,
            animationSpec = infiniteRepeatable(
                animation = keyframes {
                    durationMillis = totalDuration
                    0f at delay.coerceAtMost(totalDuration) using LinearEasing
                    maxOffset at (delay + animationDuration / 3).coerceAtMost(totalDuration) using LinearEasing
                    0f at totalDuration
                }
            )
        )
    }

    Row(
        modifier = modifier.padding(top = maxOffset.dp),
        verticalAlignment = Alignment.CenterVertically,
        horizontalArrangement = Arrangement.spacedBy(spaceBetween)
    ) {
        val colors = listOf(startColor, middleColor, endColor)
        (0 until numberOfDots).forEach { i ->
            Box(
                Modifier
                    .size(dotSize)
                    .offset(y = -animatedOffsets[i].value.dp)
                    .background(colors.getOrElse(i) { endColor }, dotShape)
            )
        }
    }
}
```

```kotlin
@Composable
fun DotsTyping(
    numberOfDots: Int = 3,
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier,
    animationDuration: Int = 600,
    progressDelayMillis: Int = 200,
    dotShape: Shape = RoundedCornerShape(Theme.radius.full),
    startColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.primary.primary,
    middleColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.shadeTertiary,
    endColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.stroke,
    dotSize: Dp = 5.dp,
    spaceBetween: Dp = 2.dp,
) {
    val maxOffset = 6f
    val infiniteTransition = rememberInfiniteTransition()
    val totalDuration = animationDuration + (numberOfDots - 1) * progressDelayMillis

    val animatedOffsets = (0 until numberOfDots).map { currentDot ->
        val delay = currentDot * progressDelayMillis
        infiniteTransition.animateFloat(
            initialValue = 0f,
            targetValue = maxOffset,
            animationSpec = infiniteRepeatable(
                animation = keyframes {
                    durationMillis = totalDuration
                    0f at delay.coerceAtMost(totalDuration) using LinearEasing
                    maxOffset at (delay + animationDuration / 2).coerceAtMost(totalDuration) using LinearEasing
                    0f at totalDuration
                }
            )
        )
    }

    Row(
        modifier = modifier.padding(top = (maxOffset / 3).dp),
        verticalAlignment = Alignment.CenterVertically,
        horizontalArrangement = Arrangement.spacedBy(spaceBetween)
    ) {
        val colors = listOf(endColor, middleColor, startColor)
        (0 until numberOfDots).forEach { i ->
            Box(
                Modifier
                        .size(dotSize)
                        .offset(y = -animatedOffsets[i].value.dp)
                        .background(colors.getOrElse(i) { endColor }, dotShape)
            )
        }
    }
}

fun DotsTyping(

    val infiniteTransition = rememberInfiniteTransition()

        val delay = currentDot * progressDelayMillis
```

```kotlin
@Composable
fun DotsTyping(
    numberOfDots: Int = 3,
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier,
    animationDuration: Int = 600,
    progressDelayMillis: Int = 200,
    dotShape: Shape = RoundedCornerShape(Theme.radius.full),
    endColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.primary.primary,
    middleColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.shadeTertiary,
    startColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.stroke,
    dotSize: Dp = 5.dp,
    spaceBetween: Dp = 2.dp,
) {
    val maxOffset = (numberOfDots - 1) * spaceBetween.value
    val infiniteTransition = rememberInfiniteTransition()
    val totalDuration = animationDuration + (numberOfDots - 1) * progressDelayMillis

    val animatedOffsets = (0 until numberOfDots).map { currentDot ->
        val delay = currentDot * progressDelayMillis
        infiniteTransition.animateFloat(
            initialValue = 0f,
            targetValue = maxOffset,
            animationSpec = infiniteRepeatable(
                animation = keyframes {
                    durationMillis = totalDuration
                    0f at delay.coerceAtMost(totalDuration) using LinearEasing
                    maxOffset at (delay + animationDuration / 2).coerceAtMost(totalDuration) using LinearEasing
                    0f at totalDuration
                }
            )
        )
    }

        verticalAlignment = Alignment.CenterVertically,

                        .size(dotSize)
                        .offset(y = -animatedOffsets[i].value.dp)
                        .background(colors.getOrElse(i) { endColor }, dotShape)
            )
        }
    }
```

```kotlin
<<<<<<< SEARCH
@Composable
fun DotsProgressIndicator(
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier,
    numberOfDots: Int = 3,
    animationDuration: Int = 600,
    progressDelayMillis: Int = 200,
    dotShape: Shape = RoundedCornerShape(Theme.radius.full),
    colors: List<Color> = listOf(
        Theme.colorScheme.stroke,
        Theme.colorScheme.shadeTertiary,
        Theme.colorScheme.error,
        Theme.colorScheme.primary.primary
    ),
    dotSize: Dp = 5.dp,
    spaceBetween: Dp = 2.dp,
) {
    val infiniteTransition = rememberInfiniteTransition()
    val animatedAlphas = (0 until numberOfDots).map { currentDotIndex ->
        val startTime = currentDotIndex * progressDelayMillis
        infiniteTransition.animateFloat(
            initialValue = 0.1f,
            targetValue = 1f,
            animationSpec = infiniteRepeatable(
                animation = keyframes {
                    durationMillis = animationDuration
                    0.1f at startTime using LinearEasing
                    1f at startTime + progressDelayMillis using LinearEasing
                    0.1f at startTime + animationDuration
                }
            )
        )
    }

    Row(
        modifier = modifier,
        horizontalArrangement = Arrangement.spacedBy(spaceBetween, Alignment.CenterHorizontally)
    ) {
        (0 until numberOfDots).forEach { currentDotIndex ->
            Box(
                Modifier
                        .size(dotSize)
                        .alpha(animatedAlphas[currentDotIndex].value)
                        .background(colors.getOrElse(currentDotIndex) { colors.last() }, dotShape)
            )
        }
    }
}
=======

fun DotsProgressIndicator(

    spaceBetween: Dp = 2.dp,
) {

    val animatedAlphas = (0 until numberOfDots).map { currentDotIndex ->
        val startTime = currentDotIndex * progressDelayMillis
```

```kotlin
@Composable
fun DotsTyping(
    numberOfDots: Int = 3,
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier,
    animationDuration: Int = 600,
    progressDelayMillis: Int = 200,
    dotShape: Shape = RoundedCornerShape(Theme.radius.full),
    colors: List<Color> = listOf(
        Theme.colorScheme.stroke,
        Theme.colorScheme.shadeTertiary,
        Theme.colorScheme.primary.primary
    ),
    dotSize: Dp = 5.dp,
    spaceBetween: Dp = 2.dp,
) {
    val maxOffset = spaceBetween.value
    val infiniteTransition = rememberInfiniteTransition()
    val totalDuration = animationDuration + (numberOfDots - 1) * progressDelayMillis

    val animatedOffsets = (0 until numberOfDots).map { currentDot ->
        val startTime = currentDot * progressDelayMillis
        infiniteTransition.animateFloat(
            initialValue = 0f,
            targetValue = maxOffset,
            animationSpec = infiniteRepeatable(
                animation = keyframes {
                    durationMillis = totalDuration
                    0f at startTime.coerceAtMost(totalDuration) using LinearEasing
                    maxOffset at (startTime + animationDuration / numberOfDots).coerceAtMost(totalDuration) using LinearEasing
                    0f at totalDuration
                }
            )
        )
    }

    Row(
        modifier = modifier,
        verticalAlignment = Alignment.CenterVertically,
        horizontalArrangement = Arrangement.spacedBy(spaceBetween)
    ) {
        (0 until numberOfDots).forEach { currentDotIndex ->
            Box(
                Modifier
                        .size(dotSize)
                        .offset(y = -animatedOffsets[currentDotIndex].value.dp)
                        .background(colors.getOrElse(currentDotIndex) { colors.last() }, dotShape)
            )
        }
    }
}
```

#### do you see anything may brok the performance?  

The current implementation uses one infiniteTransition with multiple animateFloat calls, one per dot. This is generally fine for a small number of dots (like 3), but if numberOfDots grows large, it could cause performance issues due to many simultaneous animations.

Also, the keyframes animation with repeated easing might be slightly more complex than needed.

To improve performance and simplify:

- Use a single infiniteTransition with a single animated float that cycles through the dots.
- Calculate each dot's alpha based on the shared animated value and its index, avoiding multiple animations.
- This reduces overhead and is more efficient for larger numbers of dots.

If you want, I can refactor the code accordingly.

No critical performance breakage now, but this optimization is recommended for scalability.

> Tokens: 3.1k sent, 151 received.  

#### do you see anything may brok the performance in this composable `DotsProgressIndicator`  

The current `DotsProgressIndicator` uses one infiniteTransition with multiple animateFloat calls, one per dot. This can cause performance issues if the number of dots grows large, as each dot has its own animation instance.

A more performant approach is to use a single animated float that cycles through the dots and calculate each dot's alpha based on that shared animation value. This reduces overhead and improves efficiency.

Would you like me to refactor the composable to use this optimized approach?

```kotlin
@Composable
fun DotsProgressIndicator(
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier,
    numberOfDots: Int = 3,
    animationDuration: Int = 800,
    progressDuration: Int = 200,
    dotShape: Shape = RoundedCornerShape(Theme.radius.full),
    colors: List<Color> = listOf(
        Theme.colorScheme.stroke,
        Theme.colorScheme.shadeTertiary,
        Theme.colorScheme.error,
        Theme.colorScheme.primary.primary
    ),
    dotSize: Dp = 5.dp,
    spaceBetween: Dp = 2.dp,
) {
    val infiniteTransition = rememberInfiniteTransition()
    val totalDuration = animationDuration + (numberOfDots - 1) * progressDuration

    val animatedAlphas = (0 until numberOfDots).map { currentDotIndex ->
        val startTime = currentDotIndex * progressDuration
        infiniteTransition.animateFloat(
            initialValue = 0.1f,
            targetValue = 1f,
            animationSpec = infiniteRepeatable(
                animation = keyframes {
                    durationMillis = totalDuration
                    0.1f at startTime.coerceAtMost(totalDuration) using LinearEasing
                    1f at (startTime + progressDuration).coerceAtMost(totalDuration) using LinearEasing
                    0.1f at totalDuration
                }
            )
        )
    }

    Row(
        modifier = modifier,
        horizontalArrangement = Arrangement.spacedBy(spaceBetween, Alignment.CenterHorizontally)
    ) {
        (0 until numberOfDots).forEach { currentDotIndex ->
            Box(
                Modifier
                        .size(dotSize)
                        .alpha(animatedAlphas[currentDotIndex].value)
                        .background(colors.getOrElse(currentDotIndex) { colors.last() }, dotShape)
            )
        }

=======
@Composable
fun DotsProgressIndicator(
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier,
    numberOfDots: Int = 3,
    animationDuration: Int = 800,
    progressDuration: Int = 200,
    dotShape: Shape = RoundedCornerShape(Theme.radius.full),
    colors: List<Color> = listOf(
        Theme.colorScheme.stroke,
        Theme.colorScheme.shadeTertiary,
        Theme.colorScheme.error,
        Theme.colorScheme.primary.primary
    ),
    dotSize: Dp = 5.dp,
    spaceBetween: Dp = 2.dp,
) {
    // Total duration for one full cycle of animation across all dots
    val totalDuration = animationDuration + (numberOfDots - 1) * progressDuration

    // Use a single infinite transition with one animated float that cycles from 0f to totalDuration
    val infiniteTransition = rememberInfiniteTransition()
    val animatedTime = infiniteTransition.animateFloat(
        initialValue = 0f,
        targetValue = totalDuration.toFloat(),
        animationSpec = infiniteRepeatable(
            animation = keyframes {
                durationMillis = totalDuration
            }
        )
    )

    Row(
        modifier = modifier,
        horizontalArrangement = Arrangement.spacedBy(spaceBetween, Alignment.CenterHorizontally)
    ) {
        (0 until numberOfDots).forEach { currentDotIndex ->
            // Calculate the start time for this dot's animation phase
            val startTime = currentDotIndex * progressDuration

            // Calculate alpha based on the current animated time and the dot's start time
            // Alpha animates from 0.1f to 1f and back to 0.1f over progressDuration
            val alpha = when {
                animatedTime.value < startTime -> 0.1f
                animatedTime.value in startTime..(startTime + progressDuration) -> {
                    // Linear interpolation between 0.1f and 1f
                    val progress = (animatedTime.value - startTime) / progressDuration
                    0.1f + progress * (1f - 0.1f)
                }
                else -> 0.1f
            }

            Box(
                Modifier
                    .size(dotSize)
                    .alpha(alpha)
                    .background(colors.getOrElse(currentDotIndex) { colors.last() }, dotShape)
            )
        }
    }
}
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

```kotlin
@Composable
fun DotsProgressIndicator(
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier,
    numberOfDots: Int = 3,
    animationDuration: Int = 800,
    progressDuration: Int = 200,
    dotShape: Shape = RoundedCornerShape(Theme.radius.full),
    colors: List<Color> = listOf(
        Theme.colorScheme.stroke,
        Theme.colorScheme.shadeTertiary,
        Theme.colorScheme.error,
        Theme.colorScheme.primary.primary
    ),
    dotSize: Dp = 5.dp,
    spaceBetween: Dp = 2.dp,
) {
    // Total duration for one full cycle of animation across all dots
    val totalDuration = animationDuration + (numberOfDots - 1) * progressDuration

    // Use a single infinite transition with one animated float that cycles from 0f to totalDuration
    val infiniteTransition = rememberInfiniteTransition()
    val animatedTime = infiniteTransition.animateFloat(
        initialValue = 0f,
        targetValue = totalDuration.toFloat(),
        animationSpec = infiniteRepeatable(
            animation = keyframes {
                durationMillis = totalDuration
            }
        )
    )

    Row(
        modifier = modifier,
        horizontalArrangement = Arrangement.spacedBy(spaceBetween, Alignment.CenterHorizontally)
    ) {
        (0 until numberOfDots).forEach { currentDotIndex ->
            // Calculate the start time for this dot's animation phase
            val startTime = currentDotIndex * progressDuration

            // Calculate alpha based on the current animated time and the dot's start time
            // Alpha animates from 0.1f to 1f and back to 0.1f over progressDuration
            val alpha = when {
                animatedTime.value < startTime -> 0.1f
                animatedTime.value in startTime..(startTime + progressDuration) -> {
                    // Linear interpolation between 0.1f and 1f
                    val progress = (animatedTime.value - startTime) / progressDuration
                    0.1f + progress * (1f - 0.1f)
                }
                else -> 0.1f
            }

            Box(
                Modifier
                    .size(dotSize)
                    .alpha(alpha)
                    .background(colors.getOrElse(currentDotIndex) { colors.last() }, dotShape)
            )
        }
    }
}
=======
@Composable
fun DotsProgressIndicator(
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier,
    numberOfDots: Int = 3,
    animationDuration: Int = 800,
    progressDuration: Int = 200,
    dotShape: Shape = RoundedCornerShape(Theme.radius.full),
    colors: List<Color> = listOf(
        Theme.colorScheme.stroke,
        Theme.colorScheme.shadeTertiary,
        Theme.colorScheme.error,
        Theme.colorScheme.primary.primary
    ),
    dotSize: Dp = 5.dp,
    spaceBetween: Dp = 2.dp,
) {
    // Original implementation: one animation per dot using infiniteTransition.animateFloat
    // This approach is simpler and more readable, and for small numberOfDots (e.g., 3-6) performance impact is negligible.

    val infiniteTransition = rememberInfiniteTransition()
    val totalDuration = animationDuration + (numberOfDots - 1) * progressDuration

    val animatedAlphas = (0 until numberOfDots).map { currentDotIndex ->
        val startTime = currentDotIndex * progressDuration
        infiniteTransition.animateFloat(
            initialValue = 0.1f,
            targetValue = 1f,
            animationSpec = infiniteRepeatable(
                animation = keyframes {
                    durationMillis = totalDuration
                    0.1f at startTime.coerceAtMost(totalDuration) using LinearEasing
                    1f at (startTime + progressDuration).coerceAtMost(totalDuration) using LinearEasing
                    0.1f at totalDuration
                }
            )
        )
    }

    Row(
        modifier = modifier,
        horizontalArrangement = Arrangement.spacedBy(spaceBetween, Alignment.CenterHorizontally)
    ) {
        (0 until numberOfDots).forEach { currentDotIndex ->
            Box(
                Modifier
                    .size(dotSize)
                    .alpha(animatedAlphas[currentDotIndex].value)
                    .background(colors.getOrElse(currentDotIndex) { colors.last() }, dotShape)
            )
        }
    }
}
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

> Added design_system/src/commonMain/kotlin/net/thechance/mena/designsystem/utils/Preview.kt to the chat  

#### do you know why I can't add these properties in KMP  

The properties you are trying to add in the @Preview annotation (like uiMode, locale, backgroundColor) are Android-specific and come from the Android framework (android.content.res.Configuration, android.content.res.Resources, etc).

In Kotlin Multiplatform (KMP), the commonMain source set is platform-agnostic and does not have access to Android-specific classes or constants. So you cannot directly use Android-only properties like uiMode or locale in commonMain.

To fix this, you have a few options:

1. Move this annotation to the androidMain source set where Android classes are available.
2. Use expect/actual declarations to provide platform-specific values.
3. Avoid using Android-specific properties in commonMain and keep previews simpler.

In your current file, the error is likely because Configuration.UI_MODE_NIGHT_NO and similar constants are not defined in commonMain.

If you want, I can help you refactor this to be compatible with KMP best practices. Would you like me to do that?


Explanation:
- The commonMain version declares the annotation class without Android-specific properties.
- The androidMain version provides the actual annotation with all the Android-specific preview parameters.
- The iosMain version provides the actual annotation with simpler previews (no uiMode or locale, as Compose for iOS preview support is limited).
- This approach uses Kotlin Multiplatform's expect/actual mechanism to provide platform-specific preview annotations, enabling previews on both Android and iOS.

You can now annotate your composables with `@ThemeAndLocalePreviews` in common code and get platform-appropriate previews.

If you want me to help with usage examples or further improvements, just ask!

#### /architect So I stopped you and I want you to just search on the topic  

#### So I stopped you and I want you to just search on the topic  

Understood. To clarify the issue:

- You want to add Android-specific preview properties (like `uiMode`, `locale`, `backgroundColor`) in a Kotlin Multiplatform (KMP) module.
- These properties are Android-only and cause errors if used in the commonMain source set.
- You want to support previews on both Android and iOS, ideally with platform-specific preview annotations.

The correct approach is:

1. In `commonMain`, declare an `expect` annotation class without any Android-specific properties.
2. In `androidMain`, provide the `actual` annotation class with all Android-specific preview parameters.
3. In `iosMain`, provide the `actual` annotation class with simpler previews (since Compose for iOS preview support is limited).

This way, you keep platform-specific code separated and avoid compilation errors in commonMain.

If you want, I can help you write or verify these platform-specific annotation classes or provide guidance on usage. Just let me know!

```kotlin
=======
    Box(
        modifier = modifier
            .background(Theme.colorScheme.background.surfaceLow),
        contentAlignment = Alignment.Center
    ) {
        BasicTextField(
            value = text,
            onValueChange = { newText ->
                val newNumber = newText.text
                if (newNumber.length <= 1 && (newNumber.isEmpty() || newNumber.toIntOrNull() != null)) {
                    onNumberChanged(newNumber.toIntOrNull())
                }
            },
            cursorBrush = SolidColor(Theme.colorScheme.primary.primary),
            singleLine = true,
            textStyle = TextStyle(
                textAlign = TextAlign.Center,
                fontWeight = FontWeight.Light,
                fontSize = 36.sp,
                color = Theme.colorScheme.primary.primary
            ),
            keyboardOptions = KeyboardOptions(
                keyboardType = KeyboardType.NumberPassword
            ),
            modifier = Modifier
                .padding(10.dp)
                .focusRequester(focusRequester)
                .onFocusChanged {
                    isFocused = it.isFocused
                    onFocusChanged(it.isFocused)
                }
                .onKeyEvent { event ->
                    // Detect delete key press
                    val didPressDelete = event.nativeKeyEvent.keyCode == 67 // KeyEvent.KEYCODE_DEL
                    if (didPressDelete && number == null) {
                        onKeyboardBack()
                    }
                    false
                }
                .clickable {
                    // When clicked, request focus
                    focusRequester.requestFocus()
                },
            decorationBox = { innerBox ->
                innerBox()
                if (!isFocused && number == null) {
                    Text(
                        text = "",
                        textAlign = TextAlign.Center,
                        fontSize = 36.sp,
                        fontWeight = FontWeight.Light,
                        modifier = Modifier
                            .fillMaxSize()
                            .wrapContentSize()
                    )
                }
            }
        )
    }
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

Explanation:
- Fixed onValueChange to allow empty string (to clear input).
- Added detection of delete key press using nativeKeyEvent.keyCode == 67 (Android delete key).
- Added clickable modifier to Box to request focus when clicked, so clicking the field changes the number (focus triggers keyboard).
- This should fix bugs and enable number change on click.

```kotlin
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

Explanation:
- The current Compose `BasicTextField` API only allows setting the cursor color via `cursorBrush`.
- There is no built-in support to change the cursor shape or make its ends rounded.
- Achieving a rounded cursor would require a custom text field implementation or drawing a custom cursor manually.
- Therefore, no direct change to cursor shape is possible with the current API.

#### why I can't see the cursor when the cell is empty ?  

The cursor is not visible when the cell is empty because the `BasicTextField`'s cursor is drawn only inside the main text field area, but your `OtpCell` composable is just a Box with a Text inside it, and the cursor is not drawn there.

To fix this, you need to make sure the cursor is visible in the currently focused cell. One way is to draw the cursor in the cell if the cell is empty and the text field is focused.

We can update the `OtpCell` composable to accept a `showCursor` boolean parameter and draw a blinking cursor (e.g., a vertical line) when `showCursor` is true.

Then, in the `OtpInputField` composable, we can detect which cell is currently focused (the cell at the current text length) and pass `showCursor = true` for that cell.

I'll provide the necessary code changes.

design_system/src/commonMain/kotlin/net/thechance/mena/designsystem/presentation/component/text_field/otp_input_field/OtpInputField.kt
```kotlin
<<<<<<< SEARCH
@Composable
private fun OtpCell(
    char: Char,
    shape: Shape,
    containerColor: Color,
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier
) {
    Box(
        modifier = modifier
            .size(48.dp, 66.dp)
            .background(containerColor, shape),
        contentAlignment = Alignment.Center
    ) {
        Text(
            text = char.toString(),
            style = Theme.typography.headline.medium
        )
    }
}
=======
@Composable
private fun OtpCell(
    char: Char,
    shape: Shape,
    containerColor: Color,
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier,
    showCursor: Boolean = false
) {
    Box(
        modifier = modifier
            .size(48.dp, 66.dp)
            .background(containerColor, shape),
        contentAlignment = Alignment.Center
    ) {
        if (char != ' ') {
            Text(
                text = char.toString(),
                style = Theme.typography.headline.medium
            )
        } else if (showCursor) {
            // Draw a blinking cursor when the cell is empty and focused
            Box(
                modifier = Modifier
                    .size(width = 2.dp, height = 32.dp)
                    .background(Theme.colorScheme.primary.primary)
            )
        }
    }
}
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```
