#### Please explain to me this code and how the numbers changed because I don't see any onValueChange  

The current code uses a `TextFieldState` (`otpState`) with `BasicTextField` to hold the OTP input text. The text changes internally in the `TextFieldState` when the user types, but you don't see an explicit `onValueChange` callback because `BasicTextField` with `TextFieldState` manages the text state internally.

How the numbers change:

- The user types on the keyboard.
- `BasicTextField` updates the `otpState.text` internally.
- The `decorator` lambda reads `otpState.text` and displays each character in the corresponding `OtpCell`.
- When the user presses delete, the `onKeyEvent` detects it and calls `onKeyboardBack()` to handle backspace logic externally.

So the text is managed by `TextFieldState` internally, and the UI updates by reading from it.

If you want to react to text changes explicitly (e.g., to notify a parent composable), you would need to add an `onValueChange` handler and update the `TextFieldState` accordingly, but this code currently relies on the internal state management of `TextFieldState`.

If you want me to add explicit text change callbacks or refactor to use `value` and `onValueChange` instead, please let me know.

```kotlin
=======
@Composable
fun OtpInputField(
    numberOfOtpCells: Int = 6,
    focusRequester: FocusRequester,
    onFocusChanged: (Boolean) -> Unit,
    onNumberChanged: (Int?) -> Unit,
    onKeyboardBack: () -> Unit,
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier,
    otpState: TextFieldState = rememberTextFieldState(),
    shape: Shape = RoundedCornerShape(Theme.radius.md),
    containerColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.background.surfaceLow
) {
    BasicTextField(
        value = otpState.text.toString(),
        onValueChange = { newText ->
            val newNumber = newText.toIntOrNull()
            if (newText.length <= numberOfOtpCells && (newText.isEmpty() || newNumber != null)) {
                onNumberChanged(newNumber)
                otpState.setTextAndPlaceCursorAtEnd(newText)
            }
        },
        modifier = Modifier.semantics {
            contentType = ContentType.SmsOtpCode
        }
            .focusRequester(focusRequester)
            .onFocusChanged {
                onFocusChanged(it.isFocused)
            }
            .onKeyEvent { event ->
                val didPressDelete = event.key == Key.Delete
                if (didPressDelete) {
                    onKeyboardBack()
                }
                false
            },
        keyboardOptions = KeyboardOptions(
            keyboardType = KeyboardType.NumberPassword
        ),
        cursorBrush = SolidColor(Theme.colorScheme.primary.primary),
        lineLimits = TextFieldLineLimits.SingleLine,
        decorator = {
            val otpCode = otpState.text.toString()
            Row(
                modifier = Modifier
                    .fillMaxWidth(),
                horizontalArrangement = Arrangement
                    .spacedBy(8.dp, Alignment.CenterHorizontally)
            ) {
                repeat(numberOfOtpCells) { index ->
                    OtpCell(
                        char = otpCode.getOrElse(index) { ' ' },
                        shape = shape,
                        containerColor = containerColor,
                    )
                }
            }
        }
    )
}
```

```kotlin
    BasicTextField(
        state = otpState,
        modifier = modifier.semantics {
            contentType = ContentType.SmsOtpCode
        },
        onTextInputStarted = { controller ->
            // Intercept input to allow only digits and limit length
            controller.editFilter = { oldValue, newValue ->
                val filtered = newValue.filter { it.isDigit() }
                if (filtered.length <= numberOfOtpCells) filtered else oldValue
            }
        },
        inputTransformation = InputTransformation
            .maxLength(numberOfOtpCells),
        keyboardOptions = KeyboardOptions(
            keyboardType = KeyboardType.NumberPassword

                val digits = otpState.text.filter { it.isDigit() }.map { it.toString().toIntOrNull() }
                // Notify with the first digit or null if empty
```

```kotlin
    BasicTextField(
        state = object : TextFieldState by otpState {
            override fun edit(block: (TextFieldBuffer) -> Unit) {
                val filteredBlock: (TextFieldBuffer) -> Unit = { buffer ->
                    val originalText = buffer.toString()
                    val filteredText = originalText.filter { it.isDigit() }
                    if (filteredText.length <= numberOfOtpCells) {
                        buffer.replace(0, buffer.length, filteredText)
                    }
                }
                otpState.edit(filteredBlock)
            }
        },
        modifier = modifier.semantics {
            contentType = ContentType.SmsOtpCode
        },
        inputTransformation = InputTransformation
            .maxLength(numberOfOtpCells),
        keyboardOptions = KeyboardOptions(
            keyboardType = KeyboardType.NumberPassword
        ),
        cursorBrush = SolidColor(Theme.colorScheme.primary.primary),
        lineLimits = TextFieldLineLimits.SingleLine,

                    .fillMaxWidth(),
```

This change wraps the existing `otpState` with a proxy that overrides the `edit` method to filter out any non-digit characters and limit the length to `numberOfOtpCells`. This ensures that any edits done via `edit` on the state itself will only add valid digits in the correct length. The rest of the code remains unchanged.

```kotlin
<<<<<<< SEARCH
@Composable
fun OtpInputField(
    numberOfCells: Int,
    onEnterNumber: (Int?, Int) -> Unit,
    onChangeFieldFocus: (Int) -> Unit,
    onKeyboardBack: () -> Unit,
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier
) {

    val focusRequesters = remember {
        List(numberOfCells) { FocusRequester() }
    }
    Row(
        modifier = modifier,
        verticalAlignment = Alignment.CenterVertically,
        horizontalArrangement = Arrangement.spacedBy(8.dp, Alignment.CenterHorizontally)
    ) {
        repeat(numberOfCells) { index ->
            OtpInputFieldCell(
                number =  ,
                focusRequester = focusRequesters[index],
                onFocusChanged = { isFocused ->
                    if (isFocused) {
                        onChangeFieldFocus(index)
                    }
                },
                onNumberChanged = { newNumber ->
                    onEnterNumber(newNumber, index)
                },
                onKeyboardBack = {
                    onKeyboardBack()
                },
                modifier = Modifier
                    .weight(1f)
                    .aspectRatio(1f)
            )
        }
    }
}
=======
@Composable
fun OtpInputField(
    numberOfCells: Int,
    otp: List<Int?>,
    onEnterNumber: (Int?, Int) -> Unit,
    onChangeFieldFocus: (Int) -> Unit,
    onKeyboardBack: () -> Unit,
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier
) {

    val focusRequesters = remember {
        List(numberOfCells) { FocusRequester() }
    }
    Row(
        modifier = modifier,
        verticalAlignment = Alignment.CenterVertically,
        horizontalArrangement = Arrangement.spacedBy(8.dp, Alignment.CenterHorizontally)
    ) {
        repeat(numberOfCells) { index ->
            OtpInputFieldCell(
                number = otp.getOrNull(index),
                focusRequester = focusRequesters[index],
                onFocusChanged = { isFocused ->
                    if (isFocused) {
                        onChangeFieldFocus(index)
                    }
                },
                onNumberChanged = { newNumber ->
                    onEnterNumber(newNumber, index)
                },
                onKeyboardBack = {
                    onKeyboardBack()
                },
                modifier = Modifier
                    .weight(1f)
                    .aspectRatio(1f)
            )
        }
    }
}
```

#### Now I want to add the logic of onFocus changed in order to let the cursor jumps to next cell and so on  

design_system/src/commonMain/kotlin/net/thechance/mena/designsystem/presentation/component/text_field/otp_input_field/OtpInputField.kt
```kotlin
<<<<<<< SEARCH
@Composable
fun OtpInputField(
    numberOfCells: Int,
    onChangeFieldFocus: (Int) -> Unit,
    onKeyboardBack: () -> Unit,
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier
) {
    val otpCode = remember { mutableStateListOf<Int?>(*Array(numberOfCells) { null }) }
    val focusRequesters = remember {
        List(numberOfCells) { FocusRequester() }
    }
    Row(
        modifier = modifier,
        verticalAlignment = Alignment.CenterVertically,
        horizontalArrangement = Arrangement.spacedBy(8.dp, Alignment.CenterHorizontally)
    ) {
        otpCode.forEachIndexed { index, number ->
            val previousIndex = index.minus(1).coerceAtLeast(0)
            OtpInputFieldCell(
                number = number,
                focusRequester = focusRequesters[index],
                onFocusChanged = { isFocused ->
                    if (isFocused) {
                        onChangeFieldFocus(index + 1)
                    }
                },
                onNumberChanged = { newNumber ->
                    otpCode[index] = newNumber
                },
                onKeyboardBack = {
                    otpCode.mapIndexed { index, number ->
                        if (index == previousIndex) {
                            null
                        } else {
                            number
                        }
                    }
                }
            )
        }
    }
}
=======
@Composable
fun OtpInputField(
    numberOfCells: Int,
    onChangeFieldFocus: (Int) -> Unit,
    onKeyboardBack: () -> Unit,
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier
) {
    val otpCode = remember { mutableStateListOf<Int?>(*Array(numberOfCells) { null }) }
    val focusRequesters = remember {
        List(numberOfCells) { FocusRequester() }
    }
    Row(
        modifier = modifier,
        verticalAlignment = Alignment.CenterVertically,
        horizontalArrangement = Arrangement.spacedBy(8.dp, Alignment.CenterHorizontally)
    ) {
        otpCode.forEachIndexed { index, number ->
            val previousIndex = index.minus(1).coerceAtLeast(0)
            OtpInputFieldCell(
                number = number,
                focusRequester = focusRequesters[index],
                onFocusChanged = { isFocused ->
                    if (isFocused) {
                        onChangeFieldFocus(index + 1)
                    }
                },
                onNumberChanged = { newNumber ->
                    otpCode[index] = newNumber
                    if (newNumber != null && index < numberOfCells - 1) {
                        focusRequesters[index + 1].requestFocus()
                    }
                },
                onKeyboardBack = {
                    otpCode.mapIndexed { idx, number ->
                        if (idx == previousIndex) {
                            null
                        } else {
                            number
                        }
                    }
                    if (index > 0) {
                        focusRequesters[previousIndex].requestFocus()
                    }
                }
            )
        }
    }
}
```

```kotlin
<<<<<<< SEARCH
@Composable
fun OtpInputField(
    number: Int?,
    onFocusChanged: (Boolean) -> Unit,
    onNumberChanged: (Int?) -> Unit,
    onKeyboardBack: () -> Unit,
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier,
    shape: Shape = RoundedCornerShape(Theme.radius.md),
    containerColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.background.surfaceLow
) {
    val text: TextFieldValue by remember(number) {
        mutableStateOf(
            TextFieldValue(
                text = number?.toString().orEmpty(),
                selection = TextRange(
                    index = if (number != null) 1 else 0
                )
            )
        )
    }

    Box(
        modifier = modifier
            .size(48.dp, 66.dp)
            .background(containerColor, shape),
        contentAlignment = Alignment.Center
    ) {
        BasicTextField(
            value = text,
            onValueChange = { newText ->
                val newNumber = newText.text
                if (newNumber.length <= 1 && (newNumber.isEmpty() || newNumber.toIntOrNull() != null)) {
                    onNumberChanged(newNumber.toIntOrNull())
                }
            },
            cursorBrush = SolidColor(Theme.colorScheme.primary.primary),
            textStyle = Theme.typography.headline.medium.copy(
                textAlign = TextAlign.Center
            ),
            keyboardOptions = KeyboardOptions(
                keyboardType = KeyboardType.NumberPassword
            ),
            modifier = Modifier
                .focusRequester(
                    remember { FocusRequester() }
                )
                .onFocusChanged {
                    onFocusChanged(it.isFocused)
                }
                .onKeyEvent { event ->
                    val didPressDelete = event.key == Key.Delete
                    if (didPressDelete && number == null) {
                        onKeyboardBack()
                    }
                    false
                },
            decorationBox = { innerTextField ->
                Box(
                    modifier = Modifier
                        .background(Theme.colorScheme.background.surfaceLow, shape)
                        .size(48.dp, 66.dp),
                    contentAlignment = Alignment.Center
                ) {
                    innerTextField()
                }
            }
        )
    }
}
=======
@Composable
fun OtpInputField(
    number: Int?,
    isFocused: Boolean = false,
    onFocusChanged: (Boolean) -> Unit,
    onNumberChanged: (Int?) -> Unit,
    onKeyboardBack: () -> Unit,
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier,
    shape: Shape = RoundedCornerShape(Theme.radius.md),
    containerColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.background.surfaceLow
) {
    val focusRequester = remember { FocusRequester() }
    val text: TextFieldValue by remember(number) {
        mutableStateOf(
            TextFieldValue(
                text = number?.toString().orEmpty(),
                selection = TextRange(
                    index = if (number != null) 1 else 0
                )
            )
        )
    }

    LaunchedEffect(isFocused) {
        if (isFocused) {
            focusRequester.requestFocus()
        }
    }

    Box(
        modifier = modifier
            .size(48.dp, 66.dp)
            .background(containerColor, shape),
        contentAlignment = Alignment.Center
    ) {
        BasicTextField(
            value = text,
            onValueChange = { newText ->
                val newNumber = newText.text
                if (newNumber.length <= 1 && (newNumber.isEmpty() || newNumber.toIntOrNull() != null)) {
                    onNumberChanged(newNumber.toIntOrNull())
                }
            },
            cursorBrush = SolidColor(Theme.colorScheme.primary.primary),
            textStyle = Theme.typography.headline.medium.copy(
                textAlign = TextAlign.Center
            ),
            keyboardOptions = KeyboardOptions(
                keyboardType = KeyboardType.NumberPassword
            ),
            modifier = Modifier
                .focusRequester(focusRequester)
                .onFocusChanged {
                    onFocusChanged(it.isFocused)
                }
                .onKeyEvent { event ->
                    val didPressDelete = event.key == Key.Delete
                    if (didPressDelete && number == null) {
                        onKeyboardBack()
                    }
                    false
                },
            decorationBox = { innerTextField ->
                Box(
                    modifier = Modifier
                        .background(Theme.colorScheme.background.surfaceLow, shape)
                        .size(48.dp, 66.dp),
                    contentAlignment = Alignment.Center
                ) {
                    innerTextField()
                }
            }
        )
    }
}
```

#### could you now explain why this component returns `onKeyboardBack` ?  

The `onKeyboardBack` callback in the `OtpInputField` component is not "returned" by the component but rather passed as a parameter and invoked inside the `onKeyEvent` modifier of the `BasicTextField`. 

Specifically, it is called when the user presses the Delete key (`Key.Delete`) while the current input number is `null` (i.e., the cell is empty). This allows the parent component or caller to handle the backspace/delete key event when the current cell is empty, typically to move the focus back to the previous input cell or perform some other logic.

In summary:

- The component listens for keyboard events.
- When the Delete key is pressed and the current cell is empty, it triggers `onKeyboardBack()`.
- This callback is provided by the caller to handle the "backspace on empty cell" behavior, such as moving focus to the previous cell.

If you want, I can help you add comments or improve the code clarity around this behavior.

#### could you now explain why this component returns `onKeyboardBack` ?  

The `onKeyboardBack` callback is invoked in the `onKeyEvent` modifier when the user presses the Delete key and the current number is `null`. This means the input field is empty, and the user is trying to delete backward beyond the current field.

This callback is likely used to notify the parent component or container that the user wants to move the focus or delete the previous input field in a multi-field OTP input scenario. It allows handling backspace navigation across multiple OTP input fields.

So, `onKeyboardBack` is not "returned" by the component but rather called as a callback to handle the backspace key press when the field is empty. This enables custom behavior such as moving focus to the previous OTP input box or deleting the previous digit.

> Applied edit to design_system/src/commonMain/kotlin/net/thechance/mena/designsystem/presentation/component/text_field/otp_input_field/OtpInputField.kt  

#### is the user will need a `FocusRequester` outside or the `onFocusChanged` is enough to either change the focus next or change it back  

The current `OtpInputField` component internally creates a `FocusRequester` but does not expose it to the caller. The `onFocusChanged` callback only notifies about focus state changes but does not provide a way to programmatically request or move focus.

If the parent component needs to programmatically move focus to the next or previous OTP input field (for example, after entering a digit or pressing backspace), it will need access to a `FocusRequester` to call `requestFocus()`.

Therefore, just having `onFocusChanged` is not enough for focus control across multiple OTP fields. You should expose a `FocusRequester` parameter or provide a way for the parent to control focus explicitly.

If you want, I can refactor the component to accept a `FocusRequester` as a parameter and remove the internal one, so the parent can manage focus transitions.

Would you like me to do that?

This refactor:

- Makes `focusRequester`, `onFocusChanged`, and `onPressDeleteWhenEmpty` optional with default values.
- Moves `focusRequester` to the end with a default `FocusRequester()` so the user doesn't have to provide it unless they want to control focus externally.
- Makes `onFocusChanged` and `onPressDeleteWhenEmpty` default to empty lambdas so the user can omit them if they don't need those callbacks.

This simplifies usage for most users while still allowing advanced control when needed.

> Added design_system/src/commonMain/kotlin/net/thechance/mena/designsystem/presentation/component/text_field/otp_input_field/OtpInputField.kt to the chat  

#### is their a logic or wrapper i can make to make the otp text field more easy for the user  

I can create a wrapper composable that manages multiple OtpInputField components for each digit, handling focus movement, deletion, and pasting the full OTP. This will make it easier for users to input the OTP seamlessly.

The wrapper will:
- Render a row of OtpInputField components (e.g., 4 or 6 digits).
- Automatically move focus to the next field on input.
- Move focus back on delete when empty.
- Allow pasting the full OTP and distribute digits.
- Expose a single OTP string or list of digits to the parent.

I will create a new file `OtpInputFieldGroup.kt` with this wrapper composable.

Let me know if you want a specific number of digits or any customization.

Here is the proposed new file:

OtpInputFieldGroup.kt
```kotlin
package net.thechance.mena.designsystem.presentation.component.text_field.otp_input_field

import androidx.compose.foundation.layout.Row
import androidx.compose.foundation.layout.Spacer
import androidx.compose.foundation.layout.width
import androidx.compose.runtime.*
import androidx.compose.ui.Modifier
import androidx.compose.ui.focus.FocusRequester
import androidx.compose.ui.platform.LocalClipboardManager
import androidx.compose.ui.platform.LocalContext
import androidx.compose.ui.text.AnnotatedString
import androidx.compose.ui.unit.dp

@Composable
fun OtpInputFieldGroup(
    length: Int = 6,
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier,
    onOtpComplete: (String) -> Unit = {},
) {
    val focusRequesters = remember { List(length) { FocusRequester() } }
    var otpValues by remember { mutableStateOf(List(length) { "" }) }
    val clipboardManager = LocalClipboardManager.current

    fun updateOtpAt(index: Int, value: String) {
        if (value.length > 1) {
            // Handle paste: distribute characters
            val chars = value.take(length - index).toList()
            val newOtp = otpValues.toMutableList()
            for ((offset, c) in chars.withIndex()) {
                newOtp[index + offset] = c.toString()
            }
            otpValues = newOtp
            val nextFocus = (index + chars.size).coerceAtMost(length - 1)
            focusRequesters[nextFocus].requestFocus()
        } else {
            val newOtp = otpValues.toMutableList()
            newOtp[index] = value
            otpValues = newOtp
            if (value.isNotEmpty() && index < length - 1) {
                focusRequesters[index + 1].requestFocus()
            }
        }
        if (otpValues.all { it.isNotEmpty() }) {
            onOtpComplete(otpValues.joinToString(""))
        }
    }

    fun onDeleteAt(index: Int) {
        if (otpValues[index].isEmpty() && index > 0) {
            focusRequesters[index - 1].requestFocus()
        }
    }

    Row(modifier = modifier) {
        for (i in 0 until length) {
            OtpInputField(
                number = otpValues[i].toIntOrNull(),
                onNumberChanged = { num ->
                    updateOtpAt(i, num?.toString() ?: "")
                },
                modifier = Modifier,
                onPressDeleteWhenEmpty = {
                    onDeleteAt(i)
                },
                focusRequester = focusRequesters[i]
            )
            if (i < length - 1) {
                Spacer(modifier = Modifier.width(8.dp))
            }
        }
    }
}
```

If you want, I can provide the *SEARCH/REPLACE* block for this new file.

```kotlin
=======
@Composable
fun OtpInputFieldGroup(
    length: Int = 6,
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier,
    onOtpComplete: (String) -> Unit = {},
) {
    // State for OTP digits
    var otpValues by remember { mutableStateOf(List(length) { "" }) }
    // FocusRequesters for each input field
    val focusRequesters = remember { List(length) { FocusRequester() } }

    // Update OTP value at index and manage focus
    fun updateOtpAt(index: Int, value: String) {
        val newOtp = otpValues.toMutableList()
        if (value.length > 1) {
            // Handle paste: distribute characters starting at index
            val chars = value.take(length - index).toList()
            for ((offset, c) in chars.withIndex()) {
                newOtp[index + offset] = c.toString()
            }
            otpValues = newOtp
            val nextFocus = (index + chars.size).coerceAtMost(length - 1)
            focusRequesters[nextFocus].requestFocus()
        } else {
            // Single character input
            newOtp[index] = value
            otpValues = newOtp
            if (value.isNotEmpty() && index < length - 1) {
                focusRequesters[index + 1].requestFocus()
            }
        }
        // If all digits filled, notify completion
        if (otpValues.all { it.isNotEmpty() }) {
            onOtpComplete(otpValues.joinToString(""))
        }
    }

    // Handle backspace/delete key when field is empty
    fun onDeleteAt(index: Int) {
        if (otpValues[index].isEmpty() && index > 0) {
            focusRequesters[index - 1].requestFocus()
        }
    }

    Row(modifier = modifier) {
        otpValues.forEachIndexed { i, value ->
            OtpInputField(
                number = value.toIntOrNull(),
                onNumberChanged = { num ->
                    updateOtpAt(i, num?.toString() ?: "")
                },
                modifier = Modifier,
                onPressDeleteWhenEmpty = {
                    onDeleteAt(i)
                },
                focusRequester = focusRequesters[i]
            )
            if (i < length - 1) {
                Spacer(modifier = Modifier.width(8.dp))
            }
        }
    }
}
```

```kotlin
        modifier = Modifier.fillMaxSize(),
```

```kotlin
fun Checkbox(

=======
@Composable
fun Checkbox(
    isChecked: Boolean,
    checkBoxType: CheckBoxType? = null,
    onCheckedChange: ((Boolean) -> Unit)?,
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier,
    isEnabled: Boolean = true,
    isPartial: Boolean = false,
    shape: Shape = RoundedCornerShape(Theme.radius.xs),
    containerColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.primary.primary,
    contentColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.background.surface
) {
    val checkmarkPainter: Painter = painterResource(Res.drawable.ic_check)
    val partialPainter: Painter = painterResource(Res.drawable.ic_partial)

    val currentPainter = when {
        isPartial -> partialPainter
        isChecked -> checkmarkPainter
        else -> null
    }

    val animatedContainerColor by animateColorAsState(
        targetValue = if (isEnabled) containerColor else containerColor.copy(alpha = 0.3f),
        label = "animatedContainerColor",
        animationSpec = tween()
    )

    val animatedContentColor by animateColorAsState(
        targetValue = if (isEnabled) contentColor else contentColor.copy(alpha = 0.3f),
        label = "animatedContentColor",
        animationSpec = tween()
    )

    androidx.compose.material3.Checkbox(
        checked = isChecked,
        onCheckedChange = onCheckedChange,
        modifier = modifier,
        enabled = isEnabled,
        shape = shape,
        colors = CheckboxDefaults.colors(
            checkedColor = animatedContainerColor,
            uncheckedColor = animatedContainerColor,
            checkmarkColor = animatedContentColor,
            disabledColor = animatedContainerColor.copy(alpha = 0.3f)
        ),
        interactionSource = null
    )

    if (isPartial) {
        Box(
            modifier = Modifier
                .size(18.dp)
                .background(animatedContainerColor, shape),
            contentAlignment = androidx.compose.ui.Alignment.Center
        ) {
            Icon(
                painter = partialPainter,
                contentDescription = "Partial check",
                tint = animatedContentColor,
                modifier = Modifier.size(12.dp)
            )
        }
    }
}
```

design_system/src/commonMain/kotlin/net/thechance/mena/designsystem/presentation/component/check_box/Checkbox.kt
```kotlin
<<<<<<< SEARCH
@Composable
fun Checkbox(
    isChecked: Boolean,
    onCheckedChange: ((Boolean) -> Unit)?,
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier,
    isEnabled: Boolean = true,
    isPartial: Boolean = false,
    shape: Shape = RoundedCornerShape(Theme.radius.xs),
    containerColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.primary.primary,
    contentColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.background.surface,
    contentPadding: PaddingValues = PaddingValues(3.dp)
) {

    val checkBoxType = when {
        isChecked -> CheckBoxType.CHECKED
        isPartial -> CheckBoxType.PARTIAL
        else -> CheckBoxType.UNCHECKED
    }
//    val animatedContainerColor by animateColorAsState(
//        targetValue = if (isEnabled) else ,
//        label = "animatedColor",
//        animationSpec = tween()
//    )

    Box(
        contentAlignment = Alignment.Center,
        modifier = Modifier
            .size(18.dp)
            .background(containerColor, shape)
            .clickable(onClick = { onCheckedChange?.invoke(isChecked) })
    ) {
        AnimatedContent(
            targetState = checkBoxType
        ) { state ->
            when(state) {
                CheckBoxType.CHECKED -> CheckMarkIcon(iconColor = contentColor)
                CheckBoxType.PARTIAL -> HorizontalDivider()
                CheckBoxType.UNCHECKED -> Box(modifier = Modifier.fillMaxSize()
                    .background(Theme.colorScheme.background.surface, shape)
                    .border(1.dp, Theme.colorScheme.border.disabled))
            }
        }
    }
}
=======
@Composable
fun Checkbox(
    isChecked: Boolean,
    onCheckedChange: ((Boolean) -> Unit)?,
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier,
    isEnabled: Boolean = true,
    isPartial: Boolean = false,
    shape: Shape = RoundedCornerShape(Theme.radius.xs),
    containerColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.primary.primary,
    contentColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.background.surface,
) {
    val currentState = when {
        isPartial -> CheckBoxType.PARTIAL
        isChecked -> CheckBoxType.CHECKED
        else -> CheckBoxType.UNCHECKED
    }

    Box(
        modifier = modifier
            .size(18.dp)
            .background(
                color = if (currentState == CheckBoxType.UNCHECKED) Theme.colorScheme.background.surface else containerColor,
                shape = shape
            )
            .border(
                width = if (currentState == CheckBoxType.UNCHECKED) 1.dp else 0.dp,
                color = if (currentState == CheckBoxType.UNCHECKED) Theme.colorScheme.border.disabled else Color.Transparent,
                shape = shape
            )
            .clickable(enabled = isEnabled) {
                onCheckedChange?.invoke(!(isChecked || isPartial))
            },
        contentAlignment = Alignment.Center
    ) {
        when (currentState) {
            CheckBoxType.CHECKED -> CheckMarkIcon(iconColor = contentColor)
            CheckBoxType.PARTIAL -> HorizontalDivider(
                modifier = Modifier
                    .padding(horizontal = 4.dp)
                    .background(contentColor)
            )
            CheckBoxType.UNCHECKED -> {} // empty box
        }
    }
}
```

```kotlin
@Preview
@Composable
private fun CheckboxPreview() {
    MenaTheme(false) {
        var isChecked = remember { mutableStateOf(false) }
        Checkbox(
            isChecked = isChecked.value,
            onCheckedChange = { oldOne ->

=======
@Preview
@Composable
private fun CheckboxPreview() {
    MenaTheme(false) {
        val state = remember { mutableStateOf(CheckBoxType.UNCHECKED) }
        Checkbox(
            isChecked = state.value == CheckBoxType.CHECKED,
            isPartial = state.value == CheckBoxType.PARTIAL,
            onCheckedChange = {
                state.value = when (state.value) {
                    CheckBoxType.UNCHECKED -> CheckBoxType.CHECKED
                    CheckBoxType.CHECKED -> CheckBoxType.PARTIAL
                    CheckBoxType.PARTIAL -> CheckBoxType.UNCHECKED
                }
            },
            modifier = Modifier.size(60.dp)
        )
    }
}
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

Explanation:
- Simplified the state handling by using a single `CheckBoxType` enum in the preview.
- The click toggles through unchecked → checked → partial → unchecked cycle.
- Removed redundant parameters like `contentPadding`.
- Used `border` and `background` modifiers to handle unchecked state styling.
- Made `CheckMarkIcon` a single-expression function for brevity.
- The clickable lambda toggles state properly considering partial and checked states.
- The partial state is shown as a horizontal divider with padding and color.

This should make the component easier to read, maintain, and use. Let me know if you want me to add tests or further improvements!

```kotlin
<<<<<<< SEARCH
@Composable
fun Checkbox(
    isChecked: Boolean,
    onCheckedChange: ((Boolean) -> Unit)?,
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier,
    isEnabled: Boolean = true,
    isPartial: Boolean = false,
    shape: Shape = RoundedCornerShape(Theme.radius.xs),
    containerColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.primary.primary,
    contentColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.background.surface,
) {
    val currentState = when {
        isPartial -> CheckBoxType.PARTIAL
        isChecked -> CheckBoxType.CHECKED
        else -> CheckBoxType.UNCHECKED
    }

    Box(
        modifier = modifier
            .size(18.dp)
            .background(
                color = if (currentState == CheckBoxType.UNCHECKED) Theme.colorScheme.background.surface else containerColor,
                shape = shape
            )
            .border(
                width = if (currentState == CheckBoxType.UNCHECKED) 1.dp else 0.dp,
                color = if (currentState == CheckBoxType.UNCHECKED) Theme.colorScheme.border.disabled else Color.Transparent,
                shape = shape
            )
            .clickable(enabled = isEnabled) {
                onCheckedChange?.invoke(!(isChecked || isPartial))
            },
        contentAlignment = Alignment.Center
    ) {
        when (currentState) {
            CheckBoxType.CHECKED -> CheckMarkIcon(iconColor = contentColor)
            CheckBoxType.PARTIAL -> HorizontalDivider(
                modifier = Modifier
                    .padding(horizontal = 4.dp)
                    .background(contentColor)
            )

            CheckBoxType.UNCHECKED -> {} // empty box
        }
    }
}
=======
@Composable
fun Checkbox(
    isChecked: Boolean,
    onCheckedChange: ((Boolean) -> Unit)?,
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier,
    isEnabled: Boolean = true,
    isPartial: Boolean = false,
    shape: Shape = RoundedCornerShape(Theme.radius.xs),
    containerColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.primary.primary,
    contentColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.background.surface,
) {
    // Represent states as Int: 0 = unchecked, 1 = checked, 2 = partial
    val stateValue = when {
        isPartial -> 2
        isChecked -> 1
        else -> 0
    }

    // Map stateValue to background color, border width, and content composable
    val backgroundColor = if (stateValue == 0) Theme.colorScheme.background.surface else containerColor
    val borderWidth = if (stateValue == 0) 1.dp else 0.dp
    val borderColor = if (stateValue == 0) Theme.colorScheme.border.disabled else Color.Transparent

    Box(
        modifier = modifier
            .size(18.dp)
            .background(color = backgroundColor, shape = shape)
            .border(width = borderWidth, color = borderColor, shape = shape)
            .clickable(enabled = isEnabled) {
                // Cycle through states: unchecked -> checked -> partial -> unchecked
                val nextState = (stateValue + 1) % 3
                onCheckedChange?.invoke(nextState == 1)
            },
        contentAlignment = Alignment.Center
    ) {
        // Use a list of composables indexed by stateValue to avoid when
        val contentComposables = listOf<@Composable () -> Unit>(
            {}, // unchecked: empty
            { CheckMarkIcon(iconColor = contentColor) }, // checked
            {
                HorizontalDivider(
                    modifier = Modifier
                        .padding(horizontal = 4.dp)
                        .background(contentColor)
                )
            } // partial
        )
        contentComposables[stateValue]()
    }
}
```

```kotlin
@Composable
fun Checkbox(
    isChecked: Boolean,
    onCheckedChange: ((Boolean) -> Unit)?,
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier,
    isEnabled: Boolean = true,
    isPartial: Boolean = false,
    shape: Shape = RoundedCornerShape(Theme.radius.xs),
    containerColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.primary.primary,
    contentColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.background.surface,
) {
    // Represent states as Int: 0 = unchecked, 1 = checked, 2 = partial
    val stateValue = (isPartial.toInt() * 2) + (isChecked.toInt())
```

    // Map stateValue to background color, border width, and content composable
    val backgroundColor = if (stateValue == 0) Theme.colorScheme.background.surface else containerColor
    val borderWidth = if (stateValue == 0) 1.dp else 0.dp
    val borderColor = if (stateValue == 0) Theme.colorScheme.border.disabled else Color.Transparent

    Box(
        modifier = modifier
            .size(18.dp)
            .background(color = backgroundColor, shape = shape)
            .border(width = borderWidth, color = borderColor, shape = shape)
            .clickable(enabled = isEnabled) {
                // Cycle through states: unchecked -> checked -> partial -> unchecked
                val nextState = (stateValue + 1) % 3
                onCheckedChange?.invoke(nextState == 1)
            },
        contentAlignment = Alignment.Center
    ) {
        // Use a list of composables indexed by stateValue to avoid when

```kotlin
@Composable
fun Checkbox(
    checked: Boolean,
    onCheckedChange: ((Boolean) -> Unit)?,
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier,
    enabled: Boolean = true,
    indeterminate: Boolean = false,
    shape: Shape = RoundedCornerShape(Theme.radius.xs),
    checkedContainerColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.primary.primary,
    uncheckedContentColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.background.surface,
) {
    val checkboxState by derivedStateOf {
        when {
            indeterminate -> CheckBoxType.PARTIAL
            checked -> CheckBoxType.CHECKED
            else -> CheckBoxType.UNCHECKED
        }
    }

    Box(
        modifier = modifier
            .size(18.dp)
            .background(
                color = if (checkboxState == CheckBoxType.UNCHECKED) uncheckedContentColor else checkedContainerColor,
                shape = shape
            )
            .border(
                width = if (checkboxState == CheckBoxType.UNCHECKED) 1.dp else 0.dp,
                color = if (checkboxState == CheckBoxType.UNCHECKED) Theme.colorScheme.border.disabled else Color.Transparent,
                shape = shape
            )
            .clickable(enabled = enabled) {
                onCheckedChange?.invoke(!(checked || indeterminate))
            },
        contentAlignment = Alignment.Center
    ) {
        when (checkboxState) {
            CheckBoxType.CHECKED -> CheckMarkIcon(iconColor = uncheckedContentColor)
            CheckBoxType.PARTIAL -> HorizontalDivider(
                modifier = Modifier
                    .padding(horizontal = 4.dp)
                    .background(uncheckedContentColor)
            )

            CheckBoxType.UNCHECKED -> {} // empty box
        }
    }
}
```

```kotlin
                color = if (checkboxState == CheckBoxType.UNCHECKED) Theme.colorScheme.border.disabled else Color.Transparent,

                onCheckedChange?.invoke(!(checked || indeterminate))

            CheckBoxType.CHECKED -> CheckMarkIcon(iconColor = uncheckedContentColor)
            CheckBoxType.PARTIAL -> HorizontalDivider(
                modifier = Modifier
                    .padding(horizontal = 4.dp)

            CheckBoxType.UNCHECKED -> {} // empty box
```

```kotlin
@Composable
fun Checkbox(
    checked: Boolean,
    onCheckedChange: ((Boolean) -> Unit)?,
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier,
    enabled: Boolean = true,
    indeterminate: Boolean = false,
    shape: Shape = RoundedCornerShape(Theme.radius.xs),
    checkedContainerColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.primary.primary,
    uncheckedContentColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.background.surface,
) {
    val checkboxState = remember {
        when {
            checked -> CheckBoxType.CHECKED
            indeterminate -> CheckBoxType.PARTIAL
            else -> CheckBoxType.UNCHECKED
        }
    }

    Box(
        modifier = modifier
            .size(18.dp)
            .background(
                color = if (checkboxState == CheckBoxType.UNCHECKED) uncheckedContentColor else checkedContainerColor,
                shape = shape
            )
            .border(
                width = if (checkboxState == CheckBoxType.UNCHECKED) 1.dp else 0.dp,
                color = if (checkboxState == CheckBoxType.UNCHECKED) Theme.colorScheme.border.disabled else Color.Transparent,
                shape = shape
            )
            .clip(shape)
            .clickable(enabled = enabled, role = Role.Checkbox) {
                onCheckedChange?.invoke(!checked)
            },
        contentAlignment = Alignment.Center
    ) {
        when (checkboxState) {
            CheckBoxType.CHECKED -> CheckMarkIcon(iconColor = uncheckedContentColor)
            CheckBoxType.PARTIAL -> HorizontalDivider(
                modifier = Modifier
                    .padding(horizontal = 4.dp)
                    .background(uncheckedContentColor)
            )

            CheckBoxType.UNCHECKED -> {}
        }
    }
}
=======
@Composable
fun Checkbox(
    checked: Boolean,
    onCheckedChange: ((Boolean) -> Unit)?,
    modifier: Modifier = Modifier,
    enabled: Boolean = true,
    indeterminate: Boolean = false,
    shape: Shape = RoundedCornerShape(Theme.radius.xs),
    checkedContainerColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.primary.primary,
    uncheckedContentColor: Color = Theme.colorScheme.background.surface,
) {
    val checkboxState = when {
        checked -> CheckBoxType.CHECKED
        indeterminate -> CheckBoxType.PARTIAL
        else -> CheckBoxType.UNCHECKED
    }

    Box(
        modifier = modifier
            .size(18.dp)
            .background(
                color = if (checkboxState == CheckBoxType.UNCHECKED) uncheckedContentColor else checkedContainerColor,
                shape = shape
            )
            .border(
                width = if (checkboxState == CheckBoxType.UNCHECKED) 1.dp else 0.dp,
                color = if (checkboxState == CheckBoxType.UNCHECKED) Theme.colorScheme.border.disabled else Color.Transparent,
                shape = shape
            )
            .clip(shape)
            .clickable(enabled = enabled, role = Role.Checkbox) {
                // Toggle checked state, ignoring indeterminate for toggle simplicity
                val newChecked = when (checkboxState) {
                    CheckBoxType.CHECKED -> false
                    else -> true
                }
                onCheckedChange?.invoke(newChecked)
            },
        contentAlignment = Alignment.Center
    ) {
        when (checkboxState) {
            CheckBoxType.CHECKED -> CheckMarkIcon(iconColor = uncheckedContentColor)
            CheckBoxType.PARTIAL -> HorizontalDivider(
                modifier = Modifier
                    .padding(horizontal = 4.dp)
                    .background(uncheckedContentColor)
            )
            CheckBoxType.UNCHECKED -> Box(
                modifier = Modifier
                    .size(12.dp)
                    .background(Color.Transparent)
            ) // explicit empty box to maintain layout consistency
        }
    }
}
```

```kotlin
=======
@Preview
@Composable
private fun CheckboxPreview() {
    MenaTheme(false) {
        // Using mutableStateOf with enum is fine, but ensure state updates trigger recomposition
        val checkboxState = remember { mutableStateOf(CheckBoxType.CHECKED) }
        Checkbox(
            checked = checkboxState.value == CheckBoxType.CHECKED,
            indeterminate = checkboxState.value == CheckBoxType.PARTIAL,
            onCheckedChange = {
                checkboxState.value = checkboxState.value.getNextType()
            },
        )
    }
}
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

Explanation:

- Using `mutableStateOf` with an enum like `CheckBoxType` is valid and will trigger recompositions when the value changes.
- The key is that the state is properly updated via `checkboxState.value = ...` which you are doing.
- No inherent issue with this approach in Jetpack Compose.
- If you want to simplify or make state management more explicit, you could consider using separate booleans for `checked` and `indeterminate`, but your current approach is fine and idiomatic.
- Just ensure that `getNextType()` returns a new enum value to trigger recomposition.

No code changes needed beyond this confirmation. Let me know if you want me to refactor to separate booleans or other improvements.

> Added design_system/src/commonMain/kotlin/net/thechance/mena/designsystem/presentation/component/check_box/Checkbox.kt to the chat  

#### is having the `checkboxState` in `Checkbox` like that will affect configuration change and state in jetpack compose?  

Having the `checkboxState` inside the `Checkbox` composable as a local variable (not remembered or passed in) means it will be recomputed on every recomposition and does not preserve state across configuration changes or recompositions. However, in your current code, `checkboxState` is derived from the `checked` and `indeterminate` parameters, which are presumably state passed from a parent composable. This is the recommended pattern in Jetpack Compose: the state is hoisted and controlled by the caller, and the composable is stateless.

If you want to preserve state inside the `Checkbox` itself, you would need to use `rememberSaveable` or `remember` to hold the state, but this is generally discouraged for UI components like checkboxes because it breaks the unidirectional data flow and makes state harder to manage.

So, your current approach is correct and will not cause issues with configuration changes or state loss, assuming the `checked` and `indeterminate` values are properly managed by the caller.

If you want, I can help you refactor or improve the code for better state handling or clarity.

```kotlin
) {
```

#### why this doesn't become clickable when I first time click  

The issue is that in your `CheckboxPreview` composable, you are using the same `modifier` instance both for the outer Box and for the Icon inside it. This causes the clickable area to be overridden or conflicted, so the first click doesn't register properly.

You should use `Modifier` (the default empty modifier) for the Icon inside the Box, not the passed `modifier` which is already applied to the Box.

Also, the `clickableModifier` is applied after the `modifier` in the Box chain, so the click area is correct.

Here's the fix:

design_system/src/commonMain/kotlin/net/thechance/mena/designsystem/presentation/component/check_box/Checkbox.kt
```kotlin
<<<<<<< SEARCH
        when (checkboxState) {
            CheckBoxType.CHECKED -> Icon(
                modifier = modifier,
                tint = animatedContentColor,
                painter = painterResource(Res.drawable.checkmark),
                contentDescription = "Checkmark icon"
            )

            CheckBoxType.PARTIAL -> HorizontalDivider(
                thickness = 2.dp,
                color = colors.contentColor,
                modifier = Modifier
                    .size(10.dp, 2.dp)
                    .clip(RoundedCornerShape(Theme.radius.xxs))
            )

            CheckBoxType.UNCHECKED -> {}
        }
=======

            CheckBoxType.CHECKED -> Icon(
                modifier = Modifier,
                tint = animatedContentColor,
                painter = painterResource(Res.drawable.checkmark),
                contentDescription = "Checkmark icon"
            )

            CheckBoxType.PARTIAL -> HorizontalDivider(
                thickness = 2.dp,
                color = colors.contentColor,
                modifier = Modifier
                    .size(10.dp, 2.dp)
                    .clip(RoundedCornerShape(Theme.radius.xxs))
            )

            CheckBoxType.UNCHECKED -> {}
        }
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

This change ensures the clickable area is not interfered with by the Icon's modifier.

Try this fix and your checkbox should become clickable on the first click.

```kotlin
@Preview
@Composable
private fun CheckboxPreview() {
```

```kotlin
@Preview
fun App() {
    MenaTheme(false) {
        val checkboxState = remember { mutableStateOf(CheckBoxType.CHECKED) }
        var isEnabled by remember { mutableStateOf(false) }
```

#### /add /Users/user/AndroidStudioProjects/MENA-mobile/composeApp/src/commonMain/kotlin/net/thechance/mena/App.kt  
> Added composeApp/src/commonMain/kotlin/net/thechance/mena/App.kt to the chat  

#### I think the problem is here when I click it doesn't becomes enabled please find the issue  

The issue is that the Checkbox is inside a Box, but the Box is not the only content inside the MenaTheme. The Box and the Checkbox are siblings to the AppLogger.d call, so the Box is not the only content in the Composable, and the state changes are not triggering recomposition properly.

To fix this, wrap the Box and the AppLogger.d call inside a Column or another container so that the state changes trigger recomposition correctly and the UI updates.

Here is the fix:

composeApp/src/commonMain/kotlin/net/thechance/mena/App.kt
```kotlin
<<<<<<< SEARCH
    MenaTheme(false) {
        var checkboxState by remember { mutableStateOf(CheckBoxType.CHECKED) }
        var isEnabled by remember { mutableStateOf(false) }

        Box(
            modifier = Modifier.fillMaxSize(),
            contentAlignment = Alignment.Center
        ){
            Checkbox(
                isChecked = checkboxState == CheckBoxType.CHECKED,
                isPartial = checkboxState == CheckBoxType.PARTIAL,
                isEnabled = isEnabled,
                onCheckedChange = {
                    isEnabled = true
                    checkboxState = checkboxState.getNextType()
                },
            )
        }

        AppLogger.d("button enabled: $isEnabled", "nb")
    }
=======
    MenaTheme(false) {
        var checkboxState by remember { mutableStateOf(CheckBoxType.CHECKED) }
        var isEnabled by remember { mutableStateOf(false) }

        Column(
            modifier = Modifier.fillMaxSize(),
            horizontalAlignment = Alignment.CenterHorizontally,
            verticalArrangement = androidx.compose.foundation.layout.Arrangement.Center
        ) {
            Box(
                modifier = Modifier.fillMaxSize(),
                contentAlignment = Alignment.Center
            ){
                Checkbox(
                    isChecked = checkboxState == CheckBoxType.CHECKED,
                    isPartial = checkboxState == CheckBoxType.PARTIAL,
                    isEnabled = isEnabled,
                    onCheckedChange = {
                        isEnabled = true
                        checkboxState = checkboxState.getNextType()
                    },
                )
            }

            AppLogger.d("button enabled: $isEnabled", "nb")
        }
    }
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

#### the button doesn't update at all help please on that  

I see you have a problem where the button's enabled state is not updating as expected. This is likely related to how state is managed and updated in your Compose UI.

From the Checkbox.kt file you shared, I notice in the preview you have:

```kotlin
var isEnabled by remember { mutableStateOf(false) }
...
onCheckedChange = { currentState ->
    isEnabled = true
    checkboxState = currentState.getNextState()
}
```

This means the button is initially disabled, and only when the checkbox is clicked, isEnabled is set to true.

If your real button is not updating enabled state, you need to ensure:

1. The enabled state is a mutable state that Compose observes.
2. The state is updated properly on events.
3. The UI component uses that state to update its enabled property.

If you want me to help fix this, please provide the relevant code where the button's enabled state is managed and used.

If you want me to add a simple example of a button whose enabled state toggles on checkbox change, I can do that.

Please confirm or provide the relevant code for the button usage.

```kotlin
fun App() {
    MenaTheme(false) {
        var checkboxState by remember { mutableStateOf(CheckBoxType.CHECKED) }
        var isEnabled by remember { mutableStateOf(false) }

@Composable
@Preview
fun App() {
    MenaTheme(false) {
        var checkboxState by remember { mutableStateOf(CheckBoxType.CHECKED) }
        var isEnabled by remember { mutableStateOf(false) }

        Column(
            modifier = Modifier.fillMaxSize(),
            horizontalAlignment = Alignment.CenterHorizontally,
            verticalArrangement = androidx.compose.foundation.layout.Arrangement.Center
        ) {
            var checkboxState by remember { mutableStateOf(ToggleableState(true)) }
            var isEnabled by remember { mutableStateOf(false) }

            Box(
                modifier = Modifier.fillMaxSize(),
                contentAlignment = Alignment.Center
            ) {
                Checkbox(
                    checkedState = checkboxState,
                    isEnabled = isEnabled,
                    onCheckedChange = { current ->
                        isEnabled = true
                        checkboxState = current.getNextState()
                    }
                )
            }

            AppLogger.d("button enabled: $isEnabled", "nb")
        }
    }
}
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

Explanation:
- The original code declared `checkboxState` and `isEnabled` twice inside the Column and inside the Box, causing the Box to use its own local state that does not propagate outside.
- I moved the state declarations to the Column scope so the Box and the logger share the same state.
- This will ensure the `isEnabled` state updates properly and the logger shows the correct value.

> Tokens: 4.1k sent, 503 received.  
> Applied edit to composeApp/src/commonMain/kotlin/net/thechance/mena/App.kt  

#### why it works now ?  

The reason it works now is because the state variables `checkboxState` and `isEnabled` are declared only once at the `Column` scope and shared properly with the `Checkbox` composable and the logger.

Previously, you had duplicate declarations of these variables inside both the `Column` and the inner `Box`, which caused the `Checkbox` to use a different local state that did not propagate changes outside. This prevented the UI and logger from reflecting the updated state.

By moving the state declarations to the `Column` level, the `Checkbox` receives the correct state and updates it on user interaction, which triggers recomposition and updates the UI and logs accordingly.

No code changes are needed since you already updated the files correctly.

#### /architect think on what's the best way to let this label an optional parameter that's customizable and easy to override later  

#### think on what's the best way to let this label an optional parameter that's customizable and easy to override later  

To make the label an optional, customizable composable parameter that is easy to override later, do the following:

1. Replace the current `label: String = ""` parameter with a new optional composable lambda parameter, for example:
```kotlin
label: @Composable (() -> Unit)? = null,
```

2. Inside the `Row`, replace the current `Text` composable that uses the `label` string with a null-safe call to the `label` lambda, like this:
```kotlin
label?.invoke()
```

This way, the caller can either omit the label (no label shown), or provide any custom composable content as the label, such as a `Text` with custom style, or even a more complex layout.

Summary of changes:

- Change function signature parameter:
```kotlin
- label: String = "",
+ label: @Composable (() -> Unit)? = null,
```

- Replace label usage inside `Row`:
```kotlin
- label.takeIf { it.isNotEmpty() }.let {
-     Text(
-         text = it,
-         style = Theme.typography.label.medium
-     )
- }
+ label?.invoke()
```

This approach is idiomatic in Compose and provides maximum flexibility and easy overriding.

#### Ok beside that what do you think of the approch I'm using  

Your approach is solid and idiomatic for Jetpack Compose:

- Using `ToggleableState` for tri-state checkbox is good for clarity and flexibility.
- Animating colors and sizes with `animateColorAsState` and `animateDpAsState` provides smooth UI transitions.
- Separating colors into a `ColorScheme.CheckboxColors` allows easy theming and customization.
- Using `Modifier` chaining with conditional clickable modifier is clean and composable.
- The `label` as a nullable `String?` with conditional rendering is simple and effective for optional labels.
- The preview composable with state management is helpful for development and testing.

If you want to make the label more customizable (e.g., allow custom composables or styled text), you could consider changing the `label` parameter to a nullable composable lambda, but your current approach is perfectly fine if you want to keep it simple.

Overall, your code is well-structured, readable, and follows Compose best practices. No major changes needed unless you want more flexibility on label content or interaction.

If you want, I can help you refactor the label to be a composable lambda for more customization.
